I'm sorry i get so damn jumpy whenever someone makes the slightest
dig on LA, but i'm kinda touchy aobut the subject in case you couldnt tell

Quite frankly it hurts me a lot...

It hurts because i try to put a lot of myself into trying to make things better
into encouraging the right kind of atmosphere
and encouraging people to be more aware

i dunno.. maybe its cuz i greww up in a nice evangelical christian family
but i do think that there is a message that can be spread fromt he rave scene
i know some people think it is just about partying,
and i cant do much about that
but i do think that people can learn that there can be happiness
and respect and safety without having to carry a piece on them

whoever thinks it is right:
LA IS FUCKED UP

and thats why it needs a lot of help...
kids in LA arent going to learn that there is more to life than warfare
from their teachers, or their peers or the 50 some odd guys
on teh cornere selling rocks...
maybe its just cuz im in a college atmosphere and am deluded or something
but around me the only people i see going to help kids in the barrio
are kids who've managed to escape teh barrio
and i think thats fucked up, cuz there just arent enough...

what do raves have anything to do with this?
well i dunno.. it seems that a lot of the kids who go to raves in LA
come from these neighborhoods...
last summer there was a group of kids promoting, DJ'ing and etc
for a rad club down here...
and they and their friends were spending time setting up parties
instead of shooting at themseleves and others...

and i know of a club that was all ages that got shut down and they had
grandmothers calling up asking them to please start up again
cuz they knew that if their grandkids were there.. they would stay out  
of trouble...

yeah.. there are a lot of big scale hollywood attitudes taht float around
and try to make the scene more about being cool than doing something,
but there are a hell of a lot that arent like that
and it really sucks to be trying to do something 
for people who really need it
and get called "plastic hell"

 i hope no one's ever thought i've been saying LA is better than SF
cuz i wouldn't
i would say that LA needs more help than SF though...
and whether or not anyone takes it upon themselves to be involved with that
is their own decision...

i'm sure some day.. and probably some day soon.. i'll say fuck it..
and move out.. move some place where it's less challenging to live
the way i want to and and i can just be in a supportive environment..

but until then...

flame-boy

"Life is more important than art,
but life is meaningless without art."
	- Karen Finley

---------- Forwarded message ----------

MICROSOFT Bids to Acquire Catholic Church

By Hank Vorjes

VATICAN CITY (AP) -- In a joint press conference in St. Peter's Square
this morning, MICROSOFT Corp. and the Vatican announced that the
Redmond software giant will acquire the Roman Catholic Church in
exchange for an unspecified number of shares of MICROSOFT common stock.
If the deal goes through, it will be the first time a computer software
company has acquired a major world religion.

With the acquisition, Pope John Paul II will become the senior
vice-president of the combined company's new Religious Software
Division, while MICROSOFT senior vice-presidents Michael Maples and
Steven Ballmer will be invested in the College of Cardinals, said
MICROSOFT Chairman Bill Gates.

"We expect a lot of growth in the religious market in the next five to
ten years," said Gates. "The combined resources of MICROSOFT and the
Catholic Church will allow us to make religion easier and more fun for
a broader range of people."

Through the MICROSOFT Network, the company's new on-line service, "we
will make the sacraments available on-line for the first time" and
revive the popular pre-Counter-Reformation practice of selling
indulgences, said Gates. "You can get Communion, confess your sins,
receive absolution -- even reduce your time in Purgatory -- all without
leaving your home."

A new software application, MICROSOFT Church, will include a macro
language which you can program to download heavenly graces
automatically while you are away from your computer.

An estimated 17,000 people attended the announcement in St Peter's
Square, watching on a 60-foot screen as comedian Don Novello -- in
character as Father Guido Sarducci -- hosted the event, which was
broadcast by satellite to 700 sites worldwide.

Pope John Paul II said little during the announcement. When Novello
chided Gates, "Now I guess you get to wear one of these pointy hats,"
the crowd roared, but the pontiff's smile seemed strained.

The deal grants MICROSOFT exclusive electronic rights to the Bible and
the Vatican's prized art collection, which includes works by such
masters as Michelangelo and Da Vinci. But critics say MICROSOFT will
face stiff challenges if it attempts to limit competitors' access to
these key intellectual properties.

"The Jewish people invented the look and feel of the holy scriptures,"
said Rabbi David Gottschalk of Philadelphia. "You take the parting of
the Red Sea -- we had that thousands of years before the Catholics came
on the scene."

But others argue that the Catholic and Jewish faiths both draw on a
common Abrahamic heritage. "The Catholic Church has just been more
successful in marketing it to a larger audience," notes Notre Dame
theologian Father Kenneth Madigan. Over the last 2,000 years, the
Catholic Church's market share has increased dramatically, while
Judaism, which was the first to offer many of the concepts now touted
by Christianity, lags behind.

Historically, the Church has a reputation as an aggressive competitor,
leading crusades to pressure people to upgrade to Catholicism, and
entering into exclusive licensing arrangements in various kingdoms
whereby all subjects were instilled with Catholicism, whether or not
they planned to use it. Today Christianity is available from several
denominations, but the Catholic version is still the most widely used.
The Church's mission is to reach "the four corners of the earth,"
echoing MICROSOFT's vision of "a computer on every desktop and in every 
home".

Gates described MICROSOFT's long-term strategy to develop a scalable
religious architecture that will support all religions through
emulation. A single core religion will be offered with a choice of
interfaces according to the religion desired -- "One religion, a couple
of different implementations," said Gates.

The MICROSOFT move could spark a wave of mergers and acquisitions,
according to Herb Peters, a spokesman for the U.S. Southern Baptist
Conference, as other churches scramble to strengthen their position in
the increasingly competitive religious market.

This is a bit complicated:
If you're taking the bay bridge: take the 80 E after you cross so you head
to Berkeley.  Second or third exit will be Ashby.  Exit ashby and go east,
towards the hills.  You'll pass the Ashby Bart station on your right and
cross shattuck avenue.  Turn left at Telegraph and turn right on Dwight.
It will be on your left in one block.

have fun!
matt

Well it's that time of year when we are conditioned to buy
our little brains out in the spirit of giving.  Some of us out there
may purchase more that others,  upon reflection of what has become
a national tradition, I have come to the realization that even though
some retailers make obscene amounts of money at this time of year,
others rely on this time to just stay open for the rest of the year.


I'm writing this note to encourage everybody out there in sfrave land
who does the buying thing to go down and shop at Ameba this holiday season.

Alan, please don't be embarrised that I'm posting this but I know
that you would be to considerate of our feelings to ask for help so
I'm asking for you :)  Alan and the folks at Ameba have given their
hearts and soul to the Scene over the last couple of years, and they
really need to make some revenue this season in order to make ends meet.
I'm serious. (being a businessman this year has opened my eyes, but I haven't
become a republican yet :) So if you are thinking about buying gifts
(useless, sensless or otherwise) please drop by Ameba and buy something,
you will be spending money in the community and helping out a group of folks
that have contributed soooo much to the SF Scene.  Your spending dollars
may not be tax deductable but they are going to keeping open the most
Vibe ridden spot on the Haight!


				G

> 				Politically Correct Santa
> 
> 'Twas the night before Christmas and Santa's a wreck...
> How to live in a world that's politically correct?
> His workers no longer would answer to "Elves",
> "Vertically Challenged" they were calling themselves.
> 
> And labor conditions at the north pole
> Were alleged by the union to stifle the soul.
> Four reindeer had vanished, without much propriety,
> Released to the wilds by the Humane Society.
> 
> And equal employment had made it quite clear
> That Santa had better not use just reindeer.
> So Dancer and Donner, Comet and Cupid,
> Were replaced with 4 pigs, and you know that looked stupid!
> 
> The runners had been removed from his sleigh;
> The ruts were termed dangerous by the E.P.A.
> And people had started to call for the cops
> When they heard sled noises on their roof-tops.
> 
> Second-hand smoke from his pipe had his workers quite 
frightened.
> His fur trimmed red suit was called "Unenlightened."
> 
> And to show you the strangeness of life's ebbs and flows,
> Rudolf was suing over unauthorized use of his nose
> And had gone on Geraldo, in front of the nation,
> Demanding millions in over-due compensation.
> 
> So, half of the reindeer were gone; and his wife,
> Who suddenly said she'd enough of this life,
> Joined a self-help group, packed, and left in a whiz,
> Demanding from now on her title was Ms.
> 
> And as for the gifts, why, he'd ne'er had a notion
> That making a choice could cause so much commotion.
> Nothing of leather, nothing of fur,
> Which meant nothing for him. And nothing for her.
> Nothing that might be construed to pollute.
> Nothing to aim. Nothing to shoot.
> Nothing that clamored or made lots of noise.
> Nothing for just girls. Or just for the boys.
> Nothing that claimed to be gender specific.
> Nothing that's warlike or non-pacific.
> No candy or sweets...they were bad for the tooth.
> Nothing that seemed to embellish a truth.
> 
> And fairy tales, while not yet forbidden,
> Were like Ken and Barbie, better off hidden.
> For they raised the hackles of those psychological
> Who claimed the only good gift was one ecological.
> 
> No baseball, no football...someone could get hurt;
> Besides, playing sports exposed kids to dirt.
> Dolls were said to be sexist, and should be passe;
> And Nintendo would rot your entire brain away.
> 
> So Santa just stood there, disheveled, perplexed;
> He just could not figure out what to do next.
> He tried to be merry, tried to be gay,
> But you've got to be careful with that word today.
> 
> His sack was quite empty, limp to the ground;
> Nothing fully acceptable was to be found.
> Something special was needed, a gift that he might
> Give to all without angering the left or the right.
> 
> A gift that would satisfy, with no indecision,
> Each group of people, every religion;
> Every ethnicity, every hue,
> Everyone, everywhere...even you.
> So here is that gift, it's price beyond worth...
> 
> "May you and your loved ones enjoy peace on earth."
> 
> 
> 
>

Pacific went off

So I guess after a month (or longer?) of parties at the
north beach basement someone clued in and changed the lock.
Kinetic successfully used the drafty waterfront warehouse
on Friday (I heard) and Pacific gave it a shot on Saturday.

As I arrived people claimed "no soundsystem, cops etc" and
we saw this paddy wagon pulling out.

The clever pacific gang spoke to the police: 
"yeah, there was supposed to be a party but no one showed up"
police - "any of you boys doing crack?" - "oh no sir ..."
within 15 minutes the party started :-)

This was the building SRL used.  It is huge and long with
hundreds of broken windows beautifully lit by the surrounding
dry dock yards; located on the water with it's own little
spooky industrial lagoon.  They setup in the middle of the 
building and lit 2 big bonfires off to each side.  This and the
people kept the place pretty warm.  Occasionally the flames lept
up really high - sparks and ash flying toward the rafters.  

I am fast becoming a Jon Howard fan.
His stuff is my cup of tea.
I think I am already a Galen fan.
I was going to comment on the first 1/2 hour of Galen's
set but I guess it was his first 1/2 hour set.  Please
correct me if the following was not him >

Anyway, I think he started with this Hip Hop bass heavy
tribally song - this was followed by more Thumping funked up
shake it *now* House.   One song had these crazy bass sounds 
that were somehow 'lightly plucked', they were Sensitive -
Gentle Giants lounging in a House Meadow - they would hang
there and Ride on this fantastic stompy rythm.  (I'm doing my
best to describe this) basically I was Moved Out of my Head.
way way way  Way Out

I obviously did not get my dancing fix last weekend cuz I was
itchy all over for this party.  I had great hopes that Pacific
would vibe off Howard's house flavors and I'd say they did.  
This kind of all-party-long coherence is part of Pacific's
charm.  There wasn't a heavy drug presence at the party.
Lots of friendly fatties were being passed around though!  
It was free and fun.  I got some fruit (mmmm) and 
loads of enthusiastic people to dance with!!

Connected a few sfr names to faces - Ethan and galaxy girl Tracy
and I had my eyes peeled for a red cap ... ;)

Dave

From: "Glenn Fajardo (Starwave)" <glennf@starwave.com>

Subject: Dubtribe Party/It's A Wonderful Life
Date: Mon, 05 Dec 94 11:40:00 PST
Message-Id: <2EE36C49@msmail.starwave.com>

Precedence: bulk

Ah life...

It never ceases to amaze  me.  The wonders and intensity of certain 
expreriences.  Saturday night with Dubtribe and my friends was incredible!
 We arrived at the Groovilicious Love Tribe's gathering hall around 12:30am.  
There weren't many people around as of yet.  However, there was a palpable 
sense of excitement as the events of the evening started to congeal and take 
form.  

Prior to their set, I spoke with Sunshine and Moonbeam.   We caught up on the 
events of our lives since we last saw each other and affirmed our bonds of 
friendship.  These guys have been an inspiration to me.  I know that they 
will continue to be as life progresses into the future.  We watched the 
crowd dancing and noticed the fluctuation of the energy levels on the 
dance floor as certain songs and a switch of the Dj's came into effect.  
Sunshine related their worries about the attendance tonight.  We looked at 
the crowd, which numbered about 125-150 at that time.  We both came to the 
conclusion based on the very visible energy level that we had enough people 
for the makings of a wonderful party.   

They told me that they've recently acquired a Quadra 650 and some music 
software (I can't quite remember which one) and have been utilizing it quite 
a bit to refine their songs.   They were scheduled to start at 2:30am. I 
looked forward to hearing the difference in the music.  What new surprises 
did they have in store for us?

As we talked and basked in the glow of each other's presence, DJ Cory from 
San Francisco (who came up with Dubtribe) played a wicked set which blended 
funky happy house, trance and tribal choons into a cocktail that soon had 
everyone grrrooovin' and smilin'.  I hardly realized that I had worked myself 
onto the dance floor.  The place had started to fill up.  The atmosphere 
thickened as the vibe level progressed.  As I was dancing, I noticed a young 
woman (definitely a newbie) beside me just BUSTIN' IT!  We had both looked up 
at about the same time and I introduced myself.  There was an awkward moment 
as she was surprised to have someone actually come up to her and talk.  The 
awkwardness, however, dissolved as we exchanged smiles and connected on a 
level of understanding that we were where we were supposed to be at that time 
and place.

After dancing for a while, I went to the back room and chilled with some 
friends and connected with some great new wonderful people.  The atmosphere 
was wonderfully conducive to breaking down social barriers and making 
connections.  As I sat upon this wonderfully cushy couch, I was approached by 
someone whom I remember having met several times.  She approached me rather 
shyly and with some nervousness. She said that she had wanted to tell me me 
something and did not quite know how.  I set her at ease and we started  
talking.  She related to me how she had started coming to the parties and her 
progression from newbie to full pledged raver.  She talked about the times at 
the Choc-Lit Factory, a club that we ran collectively at the Velvet Elvis 
Theatre in January and February this year.  She then proceeded to blow my 
mind as she related how much of an inspiration I've been to her.  How what we 
did changed her life and made a difference.  She spoke about her spiritual 
awakening and my role in that.  All this from a person I barely knew.  I was 
struck dumb and speechless.  I was overwhelmed with gratitude, a sense of awe 
and also fear.  Fear because I always worry about setting a bad example and 
because I know my limits and fallibilities all too well.  I came to the 
realization that she had given me one of the greatest gifts anyone has ever 
given to me in my life.  This gift from her I accept wholeheartedly and with 
the purest joy.  It is said that the acceptance of a gift honors the giver.  
Inspiration begets inspiration.  She also has given me the gift of 
inspiration.  I know that what she had passed on to me will have an effect on 
the things that I do and how I do it.  I am resolved to honor her gift by 
expressing to all the people who have inspired me how much of a difference 
they have made in my life.  Life is indeed sweet.

Almost everyone immediately headed to the dance floor as we heard Dubtribe 
start up.  WOW!  Their music definitely  had a difference to it since I last 
heard them.  The music was richer, deeper, more organic.  They seem to have 
struck a nice balance between the electronic and organic elements of their 
style.  They played a bunch of new stuff and of course some classics.  But 
everything seemed new somehow.  It was wonderful.  People were totally 
groovin' and trancing.  The connections between spirits were visible, 
healthy, alive.  We were transported into a different dimension where 
communion and transncendance were possible and very real.  We were alive!

After their set, I went back to the back room to relieve my exhaustion with 
lots o' fresh H20, warm hugs and the cushy  couch.  and there I stayed 
talking, puppy piling and exchanging smiles with my friends until it was time 
to go home.  When I finally got to sleep, my dreams and my life were as one.

Peace Everyone.  Love,

Tigger
(Glenn)

Subject: past -> future
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

Checked out Kinetic on Fri, which was at the same large warehouse Down To
Earth as at on Saturday. There was a small crowd of 100 or so at around
2:30,  grooving to John Howard, who spun a great set, as did Tracy, who
successfully enticed the early arrivals to get up an dance.

Down To Earth ended up at the same place on Sat., as their first location,
a break-in unbeknownst to them, became unavailable. There were 4-5 times as
many people as were there for Kinetic, and a great vibe. Thanks to two
fires and the number of people it wasn't overly chilly. Cyril, Galen, John
Howard, and Solar tag teamed for a bit (I think) - quite a bit of acid
tinged house. Perfect.

Due to the large number of people dancing in front of the speakers the
sound was a bit muddy - too bad they couldn't have raised the tops a bit.

Around 2:30 a security guard showed up yelling and threatening to call the
cops. Galen convinced him not to by making a donation, and the party went
all night.  wonder about the viability of future parties at this site,
though. The cops evidently were cool when they came by, but if they had a
complaint I'm sure they'd have no qualms about shutting it down.

Major props to Pacific for throwing a free party in the face of adversity.

__

Happened to pick up a Cool World (everyone's favorite party to hate) New
Year's Eve flyer on Sunday. Hmmm, and people give LA shit for having major,
overdone, commercial parties? Sheesh. Umpteen page color booklet, 5 areas,
boasts of their 20,000 person capacity, patting themselves on the back in
print for offering pre-sale tickets for the low, low, price of $20. Ahem.
Well, I guess you know what you're in for. Can't blame them for doing what
they do.

My big problem, and the grossest inaccuracy on the flyer is the claim that
the KLF are playing. Oh, what's that in small letters? Oh, the KLF
experience w/Wanda Dee. This is a sham. Wanda Dee was a backup singer on
some of their songs and is trying to cash in on the KLF name by dancing
around as canned KLF tunes are played. Bill Drummond and Jimmy Cauty, the
real musicians behind the KLF haven't toured in ages and are quite pissed
at this ploy. From what I understand they're pursuing legal action as well.
It's a bit disingenuous for Cool World to take part in this farce.

Oh well, it's always fun to take digs at the biggies, and maybe their
hearts are in the right place and they don't care about the $ and just want
to expuse PLUR to a larger audience. There's always an alternative.

Joe

...make me feel good, every time...Jello, Mijos!

Well, the hemp rally got rained out on sat, and on sunday, Jovi, Todd and
moi were busy sleeping (well, they were...).But it did go off sunday....

Got an overdose of Daves on saturday (ahhh, ok, never enuf!) and got to see
Santa Cruz rave godess Tracy and met Derek (the east-bay one). I tink he's
goin' to wicked wit me.....

At Galen's shindig, tho, there were a few drunk homies stopping just short
of ass-grabbing, and this depressed my pet space cheerleader (Annette), but
as Ahmit,several Daves, Richard and several other of my referred "good
ones" showed up and sat with us, she gradually accepted the safety of their
escort and enjoyed herself. What a way to prove point!

Two of the aforementioned gluteal offenders DID find x and as their drunken
pals went home to sleep it off, they remained at least till 4 and were
strutting, swaying and at last dancing, while smiling like there were
mudskippers in their pants. And they had no more offensive behavior.
Especially after being accepted by some of us, and receiving candy. Maybe
they get the point?

Friday, well, same place as saturday, but 1/5 the people, still an
excellent party. Yes, it eeez Kinetic. They got a good thing goin', and for
all the right reasons. Warm squishies!
 This warehouse is all I ever dreamed of when I moved here. If I ever win
the lottery, I'll buy it, install a chill room at the far end (where they
got that doomed "house") and make loft for myself and some excllent
sfravers, and let it ou for free evry day. Gotta dream......

At down to earth, I saw two workers across the "industrial lagoon", wearing
the blue overalls and helmet, and one sorta hung on the fence, the other
danced and beat his butt on his buddy, a la Ren&Stimpy (happyhappyjoyjoy!).

More gathered, asked what was up (a party, U Idiot!) and were promptly
invited to a FREE party, but they turned down my invite (No, I WAS NOT in a
dress).
They seemed to think it was ok, we went on for 2 hours after the first one
was sighted.

Galen did this for free, and I saw no donation box. If you read this,
little feller, thank you so much, our crew did our best to give out as many
toys and candy and hugs to pick up any stragglers, and I'm shure everyone
was blown pretty durn well....what will they think of next?

Lotsa love,
 Milton and the E-Bee....(achoo!)

MESSAGE WHEN YOU CANCEL?!  Just a little consideration, ppplease! I'll
party this saturday, I'll smile and bounce and hug, but Allen and pals,

at the FMR, IT IS THE PEOPLE. Man does not live on Garth alone....

I'm not pickin' on you guys, ok, but I think we have to do something as a

have.  Can anyone take up this thread and get some people moving together?

Hello!

I love reading this list! The spirit of community and the overall vibe is 
awesome! I think that the stories about your collective exploits and 
activities are an inspiration to everyone. I frequently forward special 
posts to friends in Australia, Germany, South Africa...and to many people 
in good ol' SeaTown here. They are well received.

I have a few questions, though.

What is Wicked? A club? An ongoing party? Fill me in!

Does anyone make mix tapes from parties a-la-Grateful-Dead-bootleg style? 
Lemme tell ya...I got one tape from Cindy of Carlos (who melted my brain
cell by exquisite cell) but like every junky I need MORE! MORE! MORE! 
(Due to various paternal and financial responsibilities, I can't go to
parties every weekend....but I can bomb the bass in my office 8 hours a
day!) I would love to set up a mix-tape-exchange thingy or something. Is 
anyone interested in doing this with me?

What is the deal with raves in Dead show parking lots? As the only
hardcore deadhead-techno freak that I know of, I would like to meet more
people like myself. I'm kind of tired of being the only one who will jam
out just as hard to a Kraftwerk remix as a hot Chinacat. Also, most of (if
not _all_of_) my Deadhead friends think that techno is garbage. In
addition to that, most of my raver friends think that the Dead sound like
a cross between a high school garage band and a bucket of warm spit. I'm 
sure that other deadhead/techno-freaks will understand my predicament.

One project that I'm working on is bringing these two disparate cultures 
together a little more. I am part of a non-profit organization that 
sponsors arts events (read: full-bore parties in the woods) and I would 
like to work with some folks down in the Bay area on something similar. 
Last year we had a festival that was attended by 3500 people for three days 
up by Snoqualmie pass. We're doing it again next August and hopefully 
have enough money to buy land so that we can have our own site for a 
variety of activities. Sound interesting? Drop me a line...

Michael
"An Urban Techno Hippy"

Come/Unity report
=================

Ok,   all you folks who work during the week.    Come/Unity at 1015 Folsom
St was absolutly incredible.    Down in the basement,  DubTribe was pumpin 
out some incredible trancey Ambient beats that kept me in the chill area
totally tranced out,   bouncing my brains off the walls.    When the
mesmerizing music changed to the point where I regained conciousness,
I headed up to the main dance area just in time to dance to one of the most
brilliant sets by Garth I've heard in a long time.    Man that guy KICKS
ASS big time....  For a "Middle of a week" event,  the place was packed,
with hardly a space to dance.   Even the stage area was packed.  The vibe,
only known by the Come/Unity tribe was amazing.    I've still got a big
fat smile on my face right now as I write this,   as I'm taking a break
from work (which I started very early - Oh! More hours... Yummie...)

On my way back from dancing all night,  I did the usual stop at the
24 Hour nautilus health club and did a killer work out... WOW!!  I feel
GREAT!!!   Now,  I'm sitting here,  cranking out code,  putting stuff
between the curlie cues {  },  still with the biggest grin that my face
can hold....     

Oboy!!  And this Sat evening is WICKED..... now,  If I can get some sleep
between now and Saturday,    I'll certainly be there.....  Just look for
the crazy idiot bouncing around with a big grin on his face,  like there
is no tommorrow....

Later.....
C. Crunch

Subject: MUSIC REVIEW AND INFOR
To: sfraves@hyperreal.com
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk


...mation Service

I've decided to embark on possibly/hopefully tedious and time-consuming but
certainly interesting and rewarding venture, which I hope you as a music
listener ccan help me out on.

I want people to be able to send email to me with the name of an 
artist/producer/DJ/album/single, or whatever, and be able to get back any of
the following:

1.A list of titles by said person(s).

2.A list of compilations they appear on.

3.Other works that they have something to do with.

4.Similar artists that they might be compared to.

5.More than one (hopefully) review of particular works of said artist or album.


I would like people to submit a review and information about albums they have
recently gotten (especially), or albums that they have gotten in the past that
they have liked.  To send such a review, it would contain the following 
information:

Artist, album/single name, and any mentionable (or unmentionable :) people
involved, or for compilations, a list of artists and the mentionable people
involved.

Any other information as to how to get the item, such as record label or
whatever.

Vague hint as to what kind of music it might be classified as.


And if you so wish to put the time into it, the following optional information:

Artists you would compare this one to, or artists that you would listen to with
this one.

Maybe something like: "This artist is a cross between..."

A brief description/review of the album/single.

A rating from 1 to 10, 10 being the best (in your opinion: music quality is an
opinion of course), of the album/single, which will be averaged in if there are
other ratings of the same album.
Anything else you might want to mention about this artist, or artists involved
in this single/album.


Right now I'm doing this all by hand.  However, in the future I will be running
it off of our internet server, and will automate it, so the format of your
requests and contributions doesn't matter.


The email address to send to is:

                        jesus.chrysler@sfnet.com

When you send me something, I will save your address unless you request other-
wise, and will send you any nw information about artists that you request for.

Hope to be hearing from y'all!
                        JC

night for me... I somehow feel the need to make up for something with
another shot.  I've also boycotted larger parties twice now in order to go
to F&F's...  This is good, but perhaps there is a balance to my raving
madness (NO relation to Space Madness)?

I have a Saturday evening crash singing rehersal for a Vivaldi piece I
haven't seen in about a year.  After possibly partying that Saturday night
(I must resevoir my energies WISELY!), I will perform the piece Sunday
evening in an "Alumni Concert" (for all singers that had been a part of
this group in present and years past, as I was).  Being in the concert is
one of those ("not to be missed") personal things, so I have a big
obligation to reserve enough energy for it.

Hmmmm...  I think I'm going to be able to swing going to _A_ party that
Saturday night.  (This much my 'great' Brilliance has conquered for his
mind.)  WHAT party I will go to is STILL up in the air.

Somehow, my body tells me that an intense sound system like what will be
available at The Gathering is more of the INPUT_LEVEL I seek right now in
my life.  Friends & Family is just the BEST, but I have shifted from a
personal_contact_needing stage to a personal_growth_from_within stage.

Hmm...  and $$$ is always a factor.  F&F will be the best deal in town --
and I can't beat the vibe...  And The Gathering will happily drain my
unhappy, non-reptile-skin-wallet/kind-of-canvas'y paper and metal money
organizer - but one fucking blast-to-be, no doubt.


Oh, I can't stand it.

Subject: Choice of Party
To: sfraves@hyperreal.com

From: "Bryce Ryan" <brycer@ultima.org>

Content-Length: 2630

Precedence: bulk

Greetings!

With all the recent angst about which party to go to, I thought I'd stick
my nose in to offer a philosophical point of view.  Precede all paragraphs
below with "IMO":

San Francisco, the Bay Area, and indeed, the entire West Coast, is filled
with lots of great parties.  The ratio of stinkers to triumphs seems to
have taken a dramatic turn for the better this year, compared to last
(a really good thing!).

There's a special kind of energy that only comes at a massive (indoors or
out).

There's a special kind of energy that only comes from a renegade done with
a few close friends.

There's a special kind of energy that only comes at a one-off.

There's a special kind of energy that comes from a weekly club.

One of the best parties I've been to recently was a massive that i thought
beforehand was going to be really sketchy (Tribal Funk at the Cow Palace).
I didn't think I could have a good time at a massive in that location, but
I gave it a try and had a great time.  Another great party that I go to
(and help organize) is Friends and Family, which has the killer vibe and
intimacy of a close knit group of friends, and which I've been able to help
shape in ways that make me happy, so it feels like "my" party.  I have also
enjoyed Space Lab, which was a fine, smallish techno party that ran weekly.
I also enjoy renegades (except when i get a ticket :-), coz it's really nice
to watch the sun rise, and see the clouds and moon and stars at night with
really nice music and friends.

I guess my point is that most of the successful parties are not one-offs,
and so it's almost always possible to catch another edition of the same
thing if you can't make it to a particular version.  So, my advice to those
who are faced with multiple parties on the same night is:  if possible, 
party hop.  But, always, follow your heart, and go to the one that most
appeals to you, where you'll be the most comfortable, have the most fun,
and that has the music, merriment, and vibe you are looking for ~that night~.
And, check out another party the next time, especially one you can't really
see yourself necessarily enjoying, and try your best to make it the best
party for yourself by inviting friends along, getting them hyped about it,
travelling together with friends, hanging out together, getting involved
in planning, and doing something fun for others at the party.  Magically,
eventually, *all* the parties you go to will be great, because you'll
have made them ~your~ party, and everyone there will be your friends and
family.
-- 
====== Bryce Ryan ========== AMBIANCE ========= brycer@ultima.org =========

Oh!!  Decisions Decisions!!!   Gack!!!   Gathering -- F&F ---  Which one?

Was talking to Martin,  who very much wanted me to set up an Internet WWW
Browser machine at this upcoming Gathering.    I told him it conflicted with
F&F,  and most self respecting SFRaver will probably not want to set up
and watch his machine at the Gathering.   But,  I thought I woould at least
mention it here.    Perhaps one can go to the Gathering first,   set up
his machine for a few hours,  then book over to F&F.    There are all
these possibilities.   For me,  I'm totally in the indecision mode at
this time.    So,  for those more "Portable" mahine owners,   who would
want free addmission to the Gathering,   going to BOTH and getting into
the Gathering for free,   certainly is attractive.  

Of course it all depends on the location of the Gathering.    For instance,
if it's at a good SF venue,  like the Armory,   or perhaps the Galleria,
I might consider trucking over there later,   and eventually make F&F or
"Party hop".   But if the Gathering is in Richmond CIVIC Ctr (A very big
venue),   I certainly won't be party hopping,  at least not alone.

The big disadvantage of party hopping,   is that while in altered state
of conciousness,  I'm not that anxious to drive very far.    But if the
Gathering is at the Galleria,  or other SOMA location,   I would consider
walking there.     Well!!  I guess we all just have to see how feasable
it is for the "Party hopping" idea.   I certainly want to go to BOTH,
but in either case,    I plan on GETTING OFF!!  BIG TIME!!

See ya all there....

C. Crunch

>It is true that providing good sound for 2000 people is a lot harder, but
>I think Martin spends alot of money to get very good sound at his parties.
>All his big parties I've been to have had very clean & VERY BIG sound that
>rattle your insides out. I was hoping to go to the next F&F, but this is a
>once a year thing and I know there will be plenty more F&F's. Last year
>was a "real rave", hopefully this year will match it. 
>                        JB
> 

Now if only spending lots of money were all it took to get great sound..... 

Martin uses a sound contractor who is *very good* and has excellent (the
best really) gear; but that doesn't necesarilly solve the problem. 

For instance, that same contractor did sound for the last Basics which was
generally agreed upon to have had horrid sound; tony himself told me he
thought it sounded terrible, as did I. Two huge stacks were aimed down the
short axis of a room; in adddition to which the main visual screens were
hung directly in front of the stacks nearly *eliminating* the high end.
There was no stereo imaging, general muddiness, lack of punch, etc. 

Another example is the trocadero. Everyone agrees that the sound system
itself (ie the drivers, positioning, etc.) there, are excellent, HOWEVER,
more often than not it too sounds like shit. I was at a Basics there, too,
where people were *leaving* becasue it sounded so bad (seriously painful
distortion across the full spectrum)...

The real problem is that a sound contractor's suggestions quite often play
second fiddle to "The Way the Promoter Wants to Stage the Party" ie, where
the djs go, where the visuals go etc.; I personally have experienced this
on numerous occasions.

On the other hand, the first Basics finale at the Richmod Civic had
*awesome* sound; it was in effect two four corner systems:

XX           XXX           XX
X             X             X

       o             o


X             X             X
XX           XXX           XX

Speakers at 'X'
Stereo Sweet Spots at o

This was awesome :)

The most significant factor is the room itself and the postiioning of the
drivers within it. The best pile of magnets can still sound like shit if
quality of sound is not the concern that drives the staging of the given
event. Sound Vision in the back room at komotion sounds phenomenal because
that room was post-designed (by sound engineers) to sound great; it is,
after all, a recording studio -- there are bass traps in every corner,
acoustical tile across the whole cieling. etc. The room has an amazing
compression (in 3d too; from the balcony the sound is even better!) and,
after more than 6 mos working that room, we've got speaker positioning and
EQing down cold...

Just mu $.02

see ya
ethan

hey everyone,

  Well last night i was hoping to make it to my first kinetic party
but it ended up in a bad spot.
  After chilling out for a few hours, bryan, jan, ernie, paul, and
jamie, and i  found the location from the party had been moved from Berkeley
to San Francisco.  It was going to be held at the warehouse right
on the bay where Pacific and Kinetic were both last weekend.
  We were one of the first people at the sight and there were three
other kids there and the two guys setting up the sound system when
the cops came. 
  We were all inside the warehouse and waited inside
to see if they would maybe go away but instead more cop cars came
and they made their way to the warehouse where they promptly pronounced
the party was over.  We thought that would be the end of it but since
there was only ten of us there the cops had their fun with us and
took all of our id's and ran them threw the computer to see if we
had a record.  Intimidation and all.  
  One kid was worried because he had a ticket out for his skateboard
but they let him go on the promise that he'd pay the ticket.  One
of the guys who was throwing it disappeared though when he found
out they were checking id's. a warrent for arrest or something.

  After leaving we made it back to the map point to see if there 
was any information but just a bunch of disapointed ravers.  ernie
pointed out that a lot of the kids looked like they were under 18
and that it was good they weren't there cause of the curfew law
(the cops back at the sight did ask us if we were under 18)
  Also the guys who were throwing it didnt come out from their house
and say anything so everyone there didnt know what was happening. 
I think that was rather lame.  They could have at least come out
and explained the situation, but i guess they were afraid they would
loose the $5 each they collected from people.
  So after a late dinner at the Video Cafe we called it a night

peace

doug ) ( dougie@netcom.com

Freestyle is basically an east coast post-disco pop/dance music offshoot.
I think there are generally considered to be two substyles, Miami (or
Florida generally) and New York.  Lotsa vocals, Latin influence, slick
production but good for dancing.  Sorta like the original garage house
styles, I think.  I haven't heard much freestyle, but I know it was
quite popular in the late 1980s.  There's still quite a bit around, but
Dance Music Authority, a DJ magazine out of the Midwest, is on a constant
campaign to revive the style, especially on radio (which is cool, I like
it when magazines have a certain point of view built into their approach
instead of taking the trade rag "objectivity" stance).  

Anyway, unless I'm mistaken Stompy will not be four well-known house DJs
playing that kind of freestyle all night . . . although with the Good
Doctah, yah nevah know :)

phred

On the F&F/Gathering/Stompy tip, and as one of the DJs involved :)
simply let me say that SF has a chance to prove it can throw three
kickin' parties on the same evening and I am optimistic it will turn
out that way.  They are large-medium-small, the crews are good, and
the crowds overlap but not all that much.  Most important, all three
have proven track records as vibe-oriented events.  If SF can't handle
this situation, what I mean to say is, if WE can't handle this situation,
how can we ever expect the scene to grow and thrive?  

Now my only question is, where are all of us meeting later for the 
combined after-party!

In some seriousness, though, of course it means that attendance at one or
all may be down some because of the other events.  But this kind of
scheduling overlap is bound to happen, and I think this is indicative of a
scene that really is opening up again instead of having dates parceled
out among a small clutch of promotional groups as has been the case.
Finally, it puts a little more of a premium on promoting each party
for the next week, which means a little extra effort to bring in the
people and sustain the quality and energy.

And that's *my* $0.02 for today . . .
phred

Preston:

I certainly wouldn't go so far as to say that I took it as "fiendish
promotional tactics", however, I *do* think it's in rather poor taste. 

Sure the sentiment may be shared across the scene, and yes, I really don't
think we're competing, but the specific use of the sentiment "Friends and
Family" *as a name* is the trademark of the party I and others have been
throwing for a year now -- and you know that; I personally gave you a flier
for one (which you complimented me on!) six months ago. Bottom line I think
you could have easily expressed that sentiment without resorting to the
phrase "Family 'n Friends".  

And as far as flattery goes; I was anything but flattered. How would you
feel if I'd thrown a "Boogie Brunch" on a sunday morning across from you;
you'd be pissed and don't tell me you wouldn't.

Ultimately, it's not that big a deal and, no, there are no harsh feelings. 
We all are, after all, Friends & Family.

take it easy

>I don't understand why promoters feel a need to run against Martin on this

Just as a matter of historical fact, we picked this date in May of last
spring, and I sent Martin email with our *entire schedule* spring, summer, 
and fall at the time.

As far as not "going up against 'x', I have to take serious exception with
this. There is a wicked every month; there is a basics, a vision or a
gathering (same promoter different brand) regularly; there is a funky tekno
tribe an organic or, now, a futur (same promoter different brand)
regularly; there is a Stompy Production fairly regularly; there is a Cool
World Presents 'x' regularly. If all the smaller promoters simply lay down
and die so they won't "go up against" one of the bigger promoters there
aren't any weekends left in the year!

And what if we're sick of hearing the same DJs we've heard for the last 
3 years? Martin told me he was gonna start breaking in some new DJs 
*at this party* looks like the same old, same old to me. And I'm not
criticising them (or him) they are *great* djs, no question. Tony is still
one of my all time favorite djs; Jon Williams plays plenty of music I like;
and yes its' true I even like Jeno upon occasion :)

BUT:

What if we're sick of paying $15, $20 or $25?

What if we prefer to party with 300 people instead of 3000?

Waht if we prefer to party with people of *all* ages.

What if we want to hear *TECHNO!*

No, I'm sorry, we have an obligation to provide an alternative to all of
the above ON THE SAME NIGHT else, it's not, there's not, an *alternative*.
And alternatives, diversity, CHOICES (pun intended!) are essential to the
overall health of everything; this scene included.

take it easy
ethan

I wasn't trying to say that you shouldn't run against Martin or big
parties, but I thought an exception should be made for a party that can
only happen on one day of the year. I was also trying to say that I
thought people should drop their personal preferances and go for the
community. The Gathering is not just any old party, it has had more
influence on the scene than anything else but Wicked/FMR, I don't think
people should never run against it, but for the 3 year anniversary, yes an
exception should definatly be made. I personaly usualy don't like big
parties all that much, my music of choice is acid-house (NOWHERE to go for
this, except home), I have some dissagriances with (but much respect) for
the way Martin has thrown parties as of late and I hate that new color
flier :) . I am dropping all this because I personaly think other people
and myself should go to this party for the scene & nothing else, $20 aint
a helluva' lot to pay for probably one of the more important things in
your life. You can't deny that there are serious problems with the scene
today. In my opinion most people newer to the scene are not given the
oppurtunity that most of us got to find out what it's all about (yeah it's
subjective, but I think the "vibe" works for most of us), if there are
enough people who know, those that don't will learn (maybe not all that
fast, but they will very quickly find out it aint about throwin'
attitude). In my opinion small parties don't work that well for this,
usualy these kind of people feel left out while everybody else seems to
have an incredible connection to oneanother. The only way to teach them is
with big parties, the problem is most of us don't have the patience to go
to these gangster-attitude infested parties and spread the "vibe". I know
there will be lots of old-timers at the Gathering, whether there will be
enough to have the energy to drop the "too cool" attitude is unknown to
me, all I can do is hope & bring lot's of energy with me.  regards,
			jb

 After going dancedless for a month , I got a lot of home chores done , 
but I'd also developed a severe itch for some techno body joy. 
 So , this Sunday , I was ready to do the Atomic Dog thing! I drove up to 
San Francisco and Berkeley to do some Christmas shopping , and then I
made it to the Oakland Coliseum parking lot by 4:30PM. After eating my
Chinese take-out dinner in my truck , I ventured out into the intermittent
drizzle , my ears straining to catch the odd snatch of thumpa-thumpa.
This was complicated by the presence of various drum circles ( plus points 
to them for playing in the rain ) and car stereo systems playing Grateful
Dead tunes. 
 I met Robert at about 5:50 PM , and we both went on the search , but no 
success . He had to go phone some friends , so I went back to my truck
to leave - this was about 6:20. 
 But - hey! What's that I hear , way over at the other end of the lot?
Like a shark following a blood trail , I tracked the sound of techno to
Atomic Dog ! Gil was mixing something tasty - it was the first time I can 
recall seeing him spin . 
 It was great to see familiar faces again - Ethan , Bryce , the Normals ,
Sun , and other folks ! I had to leave somewhat early in consideration of
getting to work today , but I hope things went well after I left. 
 See you folks at Friends and Family and Stompy!

	Larry Ching / larryc@netcom.com

Isn't it typical?  Just as soon as one person gets a good idea everybody 
wants to get into the act.  And this is how Ethen must feel.  He was one 
of the original people who founded the whole house  scene in SF and the 
night he is about to throw a party that was one of the fore-father's of 
the whole scene only to have a number of key people, who would still be 
mucking around doing lame punk shows if it had not been for him (Ethen) 
plkaying at their first parties.  Now most people would get a knighthood 
for this but instead all we get are rival parties on hte same night by 
stealing other people's ideas left right and center.  A scene is not 
founded on money but on mutual self-respect and it seems to be totally 
lacking.  In short, Ethen is experiencing the fact that most people 
involved in the rave scene in sf are a bunch of un-loyal, 
diss-respectable, money grabbing indidviduals who could not give a fuck 
about their fellow raver or their fellow promoter/DJ.  People are 
shitting on you Ethen and that is very slack.
As far as having more then one major party on the same night this is 
tricky in a city as small as San Fransisco because people's money is 
limmited as well as the fact that the music will be the same (or very 
similer) at all the different parties.  We could get away with having 
lots of major parties on the same night in London because it is a bigger 
town, there are lots of different music scenes and people would know taht 
the music at each of the different parties would be different where as 
here, because the scene is much more compact, it is far more difficult to 
do.  I'm not saying that the music or the dj's are better in London (I 
acctually think that the music here is better then it is in London) but 
the scene is deffinatly more diverse so it can, therefore, handle many 
different house scenes which can not really be done.  All the parties 
happening on that night will be small, under attended affairs and this 
will not do anyone, any favours and this is sad.  In short, 
nobody is going to win from this, especially Ethen, and other's 
(like money grabbing promoter's who have about as much interest and 
knowledge on the "scene" as the size of their bank ballance) should have 
more respect for their elders and better's and be safe in the knowledge 
that your average raver is so musically ignorant that as long as you 
have lots of flashing lights and eighteen and over door policy you'll 
pack them in from miles around regaurdless of the fact that they heard 
all of this music last week.  But then what do I know?
Yours with deep respect for Ethen,
Mr.Trippy.
keiper@itsa.ucsf.edu

Subject: Getting Down and Wicked this weekend
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com

Getting Down and Wicked this weekend
====================================

This Friday,   I heard rumor that Kinetic was supposed to have a two
room gig on Friday evening,   somewhere in E. Bay.   But I called the
number and it gave out the usual Haight St map point.    I certainly 
wasn't going to go across the Golden Gate Br (And pay $3 toll) just
to go over to the E. Bay,  so I hung around at home until I found
out where it would be.   Later on,  my friends tell me that it's been
cancelled,   and the rest is history.

This Saturday,   WICKED,  plain and simple.   Legendary in it's own way,
as it always manages to bring together the best VIBE on the scene.    

Thanx to Craig and Dennise,   I get to go with someone else,   so I can
indulge in mind altering thingies.

We arrive early,   no line to speak of,   and as I handed the ticket
lady my $20 bill,   I was expecting $5 back but got $10.    WOW!!   I
actually get the reduced price.   

Markie was just getting warmed up,   while I spent some time schmoozing
with Bill and Gaby.   I also met Ravinbird...   Among quite a few new
SFRravers.  

The Chill zone wasn't set up yet,   so as people were coming in,   I was
schmoozing with friends.   Markie hadn't quite yet got the energy level
to critical mass,  but that gave me more time to say hi to friends.

About an hour into Markies set,   I headed for the dance floor.    By that
time,   about a hundred or so were tearing it up.    It's been a while since
I've heard Markie spin,   and was quite pleased to hear a lot of new stuff.

About 1 am,   I was really getting off big time....   as I found a "Sweet
spot" where the sound was just perfect,   and boogied my ass off.    Thought
I died and went to rave heaven....!!   I did my usual thing...   Gave everyone
my energy and love,  got lots of smiles back...   

AS the evening progressed,   Jeno went on and schredded my brains all over
the Troc...   Yow!!   --   Finally,   Tomas went on with some rather strange
mix of really slow stuff and (Yummy drool!) Jungle....   By that time,
most people were just standing around,   trying to decide if they want to
dance to it or not.    Willy Wong and a few other SFRavers tore it up...

Eventually,   things progressed down into the "Housey" relm once again,   as
6 am was slowly approaching,  I decided to dance until the music stopped.

Hmmmm!!   6:30 and still no end to the music?   So I headed to one of the
Troc doormen and asked when it was supposed to end...   He said 8 am...  
Immediately,  I had the biggest grin on my face.....(Oh!  Goodie,   2 more
hours),   so headed out to dance once again to get as much out of the
last two hours of the rave as I could.   Dancing pretty much all the time
at this point,   except to get water and an ocassional cooling off 

I've still got a big fat smile on my face.....   Wonderful party...

Lookin forward to Friends and Family....  although I might stop by the
Gathering First...   Martin wants a WWW site set up....  Then after 
everything is running OK,  I'll probably schmooze around,   dance a few
sets,  and head back to F&F.

C. Crunch  :-)

Okay I think we're all getting a little carried away here...

The Friends & Family, Stompy family and friends controversy:
        This has all been taken WAY out of context, one is the name of a
party, one refers to a group of people.  The party Friends and Family has
been around for about a year, the circle of people and their extended
family known as the Stompy family and friends has also existed for at least
a year.  I'm sure we can all produce documentation to back up these facts.
The fact of the matter is that it doesn't seem like it's very much in the
spirit of friendliness and family to argue about this.
        We all need to stop dissecting every party before it happens and
just go with open minds to a show and let what happens happen.  If we all
only went to a party that had big, glossy four-color fliers then we'd all
miss the feeling we get at small parties when you're surrounded by a close,
grooving circle of people all on the same wavelength as you.  And if we all
only went to small, intimate parties we'd all miss that feeling of awe you
get when you walk into a cavernous space and feel like you've stepped into
another world.  There's  many points between these two extremes, and many
flavors of party as well.  But the simple idea behind everything is that
you're supposed to have a good time.
        It's not up to a flier to tell you how a party will be, or what the
night has in store for you.  It's up to you, to go and find that out for
yourself.  There really isn't that much confusion between parties, everyone
has carved out their niche and everyone else is pretty much aware of those
niches.  I mean if I had two fliers, one for "The Gathering", and another
for "A gathering of friends - Reunion Groove" I think I'd give myself and
most other people enough credit as to be able to discern between the two.
        We've all got a great thing going, and part of what makes it so
great is the diversity.  But let's not forget unity in the sake of
diversity.

Just my .02

Love,
matt

Subject:  1 Lost Atomic Dawg!!!!!! (1 tall Tale)
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

Hi All,

Well, if I'm not sleeping through parties these days,(I knew I shouldn't have
had that last birthday) it looks like I am missplacing them entirely. Sat.
Nite-after an X-mas party (without the X) I stuffed myself with on a
Chrisatmas dinner fit for Charles Dickens. Dropping off my ever lovely and
luscious dinner companion about midnight, I was falling asleep at the wheel
before I could make it out of Carmel, and even think about making it to
Wicked.

Ah Ha!!! I'll sleep and go to Atomic Dog tomorrow, and see everyone!!!!
Leaving Monterey at 2:00--The sun was shining, my spirits were bright.
Something told me to check my mail before I left, and YES...There were the
new Doran and Jon Howard tapes I had ordered from Ameba (Thanks Allen) I hit
San Jose, and rains came a tumblin down. This does not bode
well.........since I forgot to bring an umbrella......

(Run, DO NOT walk to Ameba to buy the Doran tape!!!!!!!!)

Any Hees......I cast myself into the Deadhead bazaare--A marketplace of the
multifarious-Guys bummping into you, muttering under their breath "Gunga
Brownies, Acid, Coke,
......Nuggetts" Always good to see youthful capitalism raising
its ugly head.....Putting America first.....I put my rave ears on, and kept
listening for Thumpa, Thumpa.....As Larry Ching and I walked around.....We
would think we heard something, walk in that direction, only to find some
maniacal bongo player, or someone's car stereo blasting. Alas, I decide to
find a phone.  For a while, as the hawkers and barker were saying "Wicked
Ale, Bong Pipes, Tye-Dye underwear, etc." I retorted, "Cellular, or Can I
rent a Car Phone?"-to which I received a host of "Get lost Yuppie Scum,"
looks.

Not finding a phone or Thumpa Thumpa....I went to Sam's Hofrau
and had a great roast beef dinner.

Continuing in "The Mind is a Terrible Thing to Waste or Get Wasted"---I
walked around to where I thought I had parked my car.  GONE!!!!! The sign
said, "No Parking-Sat.9:00-^6:00"--

Shit or Shinola!!!! I called the impound yard, where they told me
they hadn't received my car.  The crack dealers on the corner I walked by
(Why weren't they in the Parking lot?) told me I shouldn't have left a BMW on
the streets around there. I stumbled around in the rain, and the dark for
another hour until
I found my car......just where I had hidden it. I had a party in the car, on
the way home with Doran. I think I'll take a cab to F&F.
Now, where is Kommotion again?

So ends the tale of 1 Lost Dawg.......Where was the party, and how the hell
was it???????       robertj...... monterey

"Brilliant, right, thanks for calling the Wicked line...."

Wicked at the Troc is definitely a sure winner in my book.  
Ya gots yer spacious main dance flo' 
Ya gots yer stage for watching the sea of people sway and grind into oblivion
Ya gots yer upstairs ambient chill zone which sometimes pumps faster 
beats than the main flo' (not a porblem)
Ya gots yer skylights to brighten up the atmosphere in the morning and 
keep everyone going til the end.  
Ya gots yer pool table.  (Although paying 15 bux and then playing pool 
doesn't seem like a value)

Sound system - I was standing in front of stage right speaker and I'm
guessing they only send the medium to high frequencies to that one, cuz
all I heard from it was chick'ing sounds in sync with loud booms and more
melodic sounds coming from the opposite side of the room.  Maybe it was my
fresh earplugs attenuating the sounds more than my usual grungy ones...
But the good thing was that it wasn't too loud. 

I dug the fast fast fast Thomas stuff, but the extended mix version 
seemed too much.  People had this look on their faces : "Where is my 
HOUSE, bring it on BABY I want it NOW".  Well it took awhile but 
eventually the door opened and we were all let back into the HOUSE.

The vibe was great.  Lots of goodness all around.  There was a gentleman 
there named Micheal acting as smile enforcer... Right on.  I also met a 
couple, Greg and Melissa who were making friends left and right, 
spooshing them with sparkles.  Where else can you do this!  

Willis

I know that this kind of a post doesn't belong in a mailing list like this..
but I thought that it may be of interest to some.

>Minneapolis Star Tribune 
11-26-94
 
Computer cops at 'U' homed in on Apple Valley hacker
By Jim Adams
Staff Writer
 
University of Minnesota computer sleuths
tracked an Apple Valley teenager for about
six weeks - watching him illegally use their
passwords to gain access to more than 10
computer networks from Detroit to Moscow
- before police confiscated his computer
Monday.
 
They monitored the 15-year-old as he
bragged electronically to other computer
hackers about his escapades.  That included
forcing the Greater Detroit Free-Net to shut
down for a week after he penetrated its secu-
rity in an attempt to use the system without
anyone knowing.
 
But the university computer techs knew.
What's more, they say, the boy brazenly told
other hackers, as the techs electronically
eavesdropped, that he knew that they knew
- and thought it was funny.
 
"He didn't care that he was being watched,
and it seemed he almost wanted to be
caught," Frank Grewe, a university computer
manager, said Friday.  He said the youth, who
lives with his mother and did much of his
mischief in the early-morning hours, was
hospitalized, possibly for psychological rea-
sons, when police confiscated his computer
modem and software programs Monday.
 
Apple Valley police investigators could not
be reached Friday, but Dakota County Attor-
ney James Backstrom said the boy could face
felony charges for breaking into computer
systems.
 
"He wiped out a lot of critical files," said
Paul Raine, president of the Detroit Free-
Net, an eight-month-old community infor-
mation exchange that charges no fees to its
users.
 
[Page #2]
 
Hacker/ He used computer as much as 20 hours a day
 
University officials notified Raine
the morning after the youth penetrat-
ed their network security, Grewe
said.  The system was shut down
Nov. 9 so volunteers could rebuild it
and tighten security.  Raine said he
has contacted the FBI about possible
federal charges because the youth 
used telecommunications equipment
to reach across state lines.
 
Grewe said police told him the youth
had problems at home and had been
skipping school while using his com-
puter as much as 20 hours a day to
gain access to electronic mail systems
and computer data files worldwide.
He said other high school students
had been involved, at least one of
whom would be prosecuted if he re-
sumed unauthorized use of universi-
ty passwords.
 
He said the Apple Valley youth had
obtained passwords, possibly from
Twin Cities electronic bulletin
boards or by using commercially
available decoding programs.  He said
the university has more than 100,000
computer users, including students,
staff and alumni.
 
The first step when an unauthorized
user is detected is to change the pass-
word to one more difficult to crack,
Grewe said.
 
"He had a whole pocketful of them,"
Grewe said.  "We would change a
password, and he'd use another.  For
a while, we were closing one account
a day on this kid.  Most people would
get the clue we are watching and they
disappear.  But he just kept coming
back and trying to break into other
systems.
 
"He had enough knowlege to make
himself dangerous, but not enough to
hide his tracks. ... My staff would
come in in the morning and say, `Oh,
Lord, look what he did last night.'
After a few nights it became, `We
have to find out where he lives and
what he is up to.'"
 
Authorities traced the boy's tele-
phone line.  After obtaining enough
logs of his unauthorized activities -
including the Detroit caper - police
went to his home with a search war-
rant.
 
Grewe said the boy appeared to fit
the typical hacker profile: a 15- to 20-
year-old male, many who have 
low self-esteem.  "He really could use
a girlfriend instead of a computer,"
Grewe said.
 
Olaf Holt, president of the fledgling
Twin Cities FREE-NET, which is
raising funds to go public, said com-
puter hackers have their own subcul-
ture: "They pride themselves on their
ability to break into otherwise-re-
stricted spaces," especially highly se-
cure government systems.
 
Holt said hears of hacker crack-
ing a computer network's security
system every few months.  But it is
unusual for a network that offers free
access to be attacked.  Holt said most
of the world's 40 free networks are in
the United States; the first opened in
Cleveland in 1986.
 
"It is not as common for a free net to
go down, because most people think
of it as a community good, and as
such, they don't get many points in
view of their peers" for sabotaging it,
Holt Said.
 
-Retyped by Drowning Child
-11/26/94
"Errors theirs, not mine"

On Mon, 12 Dec 1994, ethan miller wrote:

> >...but I thought an exception should be made for a party that can
> >only happen on one day of the year.
> 
> Excuse me? Why is this? I'd be willing to bet a fair amount of $$$ that the

> wrong but this is awfully melodramatic....

Hmmm... (digs into old flier box) Saturday Dec.14'th 1991, are you saying
that he has to have it on wednesday the 14'th for it to be a valid
anniversary, if you did an F&F anniversary would you do it on the exact
date or the friday or saturday closest to the date, I am quite sure you'd
do the latter. 

> So the Gathering is the only source of *real* community for this scene?
> Come on. The Gathering happens twice a year, once for the 4th of July and
> once for it's Yearly Anniversary. If this is all that's holding our
> community together, we're in trouble.

Did I say that? I dont think so. Well the finale was in 4/92, so
technicaly it's supposed to be over. I beleive the only Gatherings that
have happened since then were the anniversary's, one small free one &
Gathering presents (L.F.R. & Vision). Martin has since moved on to Basics
and played a major roll in an unbelievable amount of small mostly $ losers
in 93.  

> >The Gathering is not just any old party, it has had more
> >influence on the scene than anything else but Wicked/FMR, I don't think
> >people should never run against it, but for the 3 year anniversary, yes an
> >exception should definatly be made.
> 
> More influence than anything else? Do you *really* think that?

What do you want me to go back further, I think that's kind of pointless
as it has been mutated beyond recognition since than. Yeah, there were
other major contributors (Destiny, Community, Toontown, Equinox, Sharon),
two of which were part of the original Gatherings, but I'd say Martin has
probably had more influence. You could easily argue that the
majority of the current scene was more influenced by Wally/Cool world & FTT 
and unfortunatly you'd probably be right.

> >|My music of choice is acid-house (NOWHERE to go for
> >this, except home),
> 
> I *beg* to disagree here! PLenty 'o' acid house to be found around SF :)

Yeah, if going down to Ameoba & buying "House Reality" counts as plenty.
People have a very warped sense of what is what, acid-house is one of the
few things that is not to hard for those that know to classify. Most
people can't tell the difference between real 90% pre-90 (no midi
used) rough acid & acid-trance (or whatever the hell you want to call it) 
Could you please tell me of any good acid-house dj's or parties because
I've been searching for years & have yet to find any consistent ones.    

> >In my opinion most people newer to the scene are not given the oppurtunity 
> >that most of us got to find out what it's all about (yeah it's subjective,
> >but I think the "vibe" works for most of us), if there are enough people
> >who know, those that don't will learn (maybe not all that fast, but they
> >will very quickly find out it aint about throwin' attitude). In my
> >opinion small parties don't work that well for this, usualy these kind of
> >people feel left out while everybody else seems to have an incredible
> >connection to oneanother. The only way to teach them is with big parties

> Au Contraire! Not even common sense supports this conclusion...But then,
> clearly, I'm arguing with mythology now which is always a bad decision :)
> take it easy 

Gee, I didn't know I was a fucking mythologist. Are you telling me you
wouldn't feel uncomforatable if you went to some small hip-hop party were
there was nobody but your two friends that looked or acted remotely like
you and they all seemed to be have their own lingo that was no where near
your reality & to top it off they seemed to treat you like outsiders. Now
let's change the situation. You go to a big party where there are all
kinds of people there, some of them kinda like you, most of them not, but
you don't feel like a total outsider anymore, there is definatly something
very different going on, but you kinda got a feel for it now. Unfortunatly
most of the big parties now are a bad representation of the real thing &
we mostly recruit people who think that it's all about Cool World, FTT & a
hit of E (sorry for the not always true generalization). Alot of the
people who have it in them are going to miss out. If I wasn't lucky enough
to be introduced to it 3yrs ago through some good big parties, I'd probably be
one of those people who thought raves were for stupid people to listen to
"The Prodigy" & get high. There are very few parties that can manage to
have a "vibe" & be big and non-threatening for outsiders. IMH the reason
being that most people that "know what it's about" are to fucking selfish
& lazy to risk going to a big party and trying to spread the vibe. 
	
	I'm not arguing against small parties and diversity among them, as
they are extremely important to the scene. But we have lost touch with the
bigger ones which play an equaly important part & let the $ hungry
promoters and the stupid idea of being too cool for big parties get the
better of us.  

regards,
			jb

that exists after 4AM that makes a great party. It's the stamina/staying power

mere words, but what the phuch :)

From: geoffw@nexsys.net (Geoff White)
Message-Id: <199412131733.JAA16326@nexsys.nexsys.net>
To: sfraves@hyperreal.com
Subject: Wicked
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

Ya gotta stay past 4 a.m. before you can really evaluate any party.
Wicked's tend to be like 7 mile long freight trains, they start off 
slow and take a long time to build up velocity, but they are moving
like a bat outta hell by the time they hit the kansas plains at 4 a.m.

The evening started for me at sound check around 9 p.m., I arrived
to help out with set-up.  The Troc seems to be the ideal indoor setting
for the Purple People Pusher as it sounds the best there of any indoor 
location that I have heard it in. Greg informed me that the had a blown 
crossover on one side so that at least one side would not have completely
seperated sound, hmm. Markie was to open, followed by Garth, Jeno and
Thomas. We were still fooling with the sound at 10:45 when greg as me to 
put some records on so they can balance levels (I had my records with me
at the time, I told him that I'm not very good and would train-wreck, he 
said it didn't matter we just need to get the levels set up. So I opened my
crate and went at it.  It was alot of fun playing on that monster system
and it's really easy to beat match when you FEEL IT in every atom of your
body, (fuck me that's loud ;) Any way I was having fun even though I made 
a few mistakes, around 11:10 greg comes to me and says Markies not here yet
so we're letting people in, I said OH shit! No!!!, he says don't worry, your
doing fine, (I didn't think so), so I got to play for another 20 minutes
until Markie arrived and took over.  I must say that it did get my adrenalin
going and I can see what it must be like to know what your doing and to
be behind the controls of a sound system as massive as that one.

	Markie started off with some intense and wild house, he got people 
moving and grooving, his set had peaks and valleys, I loved parts of it
and was apathetic at other parts but basicaly I enjoyed it, Garth came on
and played one of the crowd pleasing sets he's fameous for, high energy
but not extremely mind expanding, he layed the shot up for Jeno at 4 a.m.
who delivered the goods, this was not the best Jeno set that I have heard but 
it was very good and worthy of the Jeno(tm) stamp.  Can anyone say Acieeed?
Pretty soon I was cross-eyed and in a state of perfect trance, (which is
what it's all about for me), he worked it, through mountain peaks and valley
lows, the energy on the dance floor mounted and by 5 a.m. escape velocity
had been achieved, I looked around to find many people tranced and all swaying
to one rythym.  Thomas came on next and played Jungle! A lot of folks didn't
like it but the stuff he played, I really loved! Nice soulfull Jungle, I can
see how people would love to be on E and dance to this. After about 20 minutes
of this he gave up and switched to the Punk-Funk-House that he is fameous for
7:30 came and the dancefloor was still full and people still going off hard,
I love thomas in the morning, he gives you that extra boost at 7:30 to get
you through the morning! whether your driving home or to the End-Up, Thomas
will keep you dancing to the end Right-On bro.  
	All in all I would say that it was a good party for Wicked, the music
was on track though not balistic and the crowd (an _extremely_ important part
of the alchemy) was friendly, freaky and ready to party.  I think the 
troc is a good location for these monthlies, the security seems to have 
lightened up on their goon tactics and I believe the club did well at the Bar
I hope Wicked gets to do parties there again, I think it can only get better
from here.

Re: good ol days

Call this a pet peeve of mine, but all these parties are
really experiential and in the moment so I just don't buy
into this "scene history" nor do I think it is the "future"
of anything.  It is happening Now.  I don't think that
minimizes anything.  Attempts to extrapolate forward
or backward in time seem pointless to me.  The idea
of a Community coming together is a nice warm fuzzy
sentiment, great, but I don't like the idea of "owing"
something to a party cuz of it's history.  That strikes
me as absurd.  I can't imagine getting all worked up
over missionary vibing at big parties.

If you are into it - Go   
Don't expect me to be your reality
Old school mold school

On Tue, 13 Dec 1994, ethan miller wrote:

> >wouldn't feel uncomforatable if you went to some small hip-hop party were
> >there was nobody but your two friends that looked or acted remotely like
> >you and they all seemed to be have their own lingo that was no where near
> >your reality & to top it off they seemed to treat you like outsiders.
> 
> Yes, I would most certainly feel uncomfortable, but I also wouldn't call it
> a rave nor would I compare it to raves...

	I don't think the point of considering the hip-hop party was to 
compare it to as rave, but instead to take us out of an element that we 
are now comfortable in and put us in the shoes of a newbie coming to 
their first rave. Small parties do have the effect of shunning new people 
especially when the 'crowd' already knows one another. It is not 
necessarily something one does consciously either. Take an example.
	This past weeked, I finally became old enough to legally attend 
all those age exclusive things that have sat on the horizon (ie. Sat was 
my 21st birthday). After Wicked some friendds crash at my place for abit, 
woke me up and eventually took me to Spundae. The crowd seemed kinda 
tight so I found myself pleasantly surprised (I have heard so many bad 
things about DV8). But as the night went on, I noticed a few things. 
People would break eye contact with me as soon as it was made, yet after 
I was introduced to them (by a friend who seemed to know everyone) I was 
no  longer plagued by the evil eye dodge. This type of thing seems to 
happen more often at smll parties where people know one another (Yes, it 
happens at big parties, but I do not think one feels quite as alienated 
at a big party).  
 
> >        I'm not arguing against small parties and diversity among them, as
> >they are extremely important to the scene. But we have lost touch with the
> >bigger ones which play an equaly important part & let the $ hungry
> >promoters and the stupid idea of being too cool for big parties get the
> >better of us.
> 
> I don't think we've lost touch nor do I know any people who I would say
> view themselves as too cool for big parties. Some people have found,
> contrary to your experience, that they have a harder time finding vibe at
> the bigger parties than at smaller parties. For many too, what they want
> out of a party has also, simply changed. 

	But if one cannot find/create the vibe at the bigger parties, 
then they have lost touch in one sense. And if what they want from a 
party has changed, then they have moved away from what originally drew 
them to come out in the first place. In my opinion, the former points away 
from creating the energy that makes a 2000+ party go off (and thus makes 
people go "OOOOOOOHHHHHHHHHHHHHH, so this is a rave..." which makes them 
come back and dance, smile, hoot and holler...). Hmmm, this sounds kinda 
like I am preaching community service, but that is not my intent. I just 
get kind tired of people wanting a canned party that will be going off 
without putting any energy into the party (that's not meant as a flame to 
anyone on here, more to a few friends who have stopped going out cuz 
"they cannot find a vibe at the parties nowadays"). Then again, maybe it 
is better that people who are not willing to bring their vibe with them 
stay at small parties (or at home) as if there is no vibe, they will just 
sit and pout
	I myself have no preference to the size of the party (except for 
what I am in the mood for at the time). I have been to amazing small 
parties. I have been to brillant big parties. Each has their pluses, but 
being introduced to raves through Martin's first or second Visions, I 
still see big parties as good, not too overwhelming medium to introduce 
people to such wonders.... But as I said, I was weened on big parties.

dave
