Right on!
One of the things I was most jazzed about moving out here from New Mexico a few
months ago was precisely that there usually is more than one thing going off
every weekend. That's opposed to one thing going off in NM per month. Not that
the scene out there is any less "cool" - I went to some killer, albeit low-budget,
events under the breathtaking desert sky.

We took a friend of a friend who's from St. Louis to Wicked this weekend. (see "1st
wicked") From what she said, the scene in St. Louis sounds very low-attitude,
high-energy and high-enthusiasm. Yet she's probably moving to SF in a few weeks
specifically because of the critical mass of the scene here.

I don't sense that any of the promotors of the upcoming three parties are
engaging in spiteful competition. Likewise, even though I'm definately going to
F&F and probably staying there all night, why on earth would I have a problem
with someone else choosing to go to one of the other two and stay there? I think
some of you are taking this "tribalism" thing a tad too far.

Peace!
-nate

PSSS - more reviews! - especially newbie lurker folks and first time

--------------------------------------
Geez, Dave! My eyes started watering trying to contain my laughter in this
normally quiet office space.

Could you be talking about ME?

I've heard lots about Wicked, so I was eager to go and see for myself. 

Earlier in the week, an adamantly-non-raver friend called and said they had a
friend visiting from St. Louis who wanted to go to a certain "big rave." I'd
heard that Wicked tours, so I asked if that was what she was thinking of. Yes,
and she'd be really bummed if she left SF without going. Well, how could Lisa
and I pass up the opportunity to show the town to someone when we've only been
here three months ourselves?

We got to SF at about 12, speeding from an early-evening Christmas party. When
we picked up Rebecca from St. Louis, it turns out she's more plugged into the scene
here than we'd anticipated ("I called Mark Farina before I left, but he's in
Brazil..."). Really nice, though, and gave us some interesting insights on the
mid-west scene.

I was a little disappointed to find that it was at the Troc, since all of the
events we've been to here have either been in warehouses or at the Troc.
However, once we got there, the sound was set up nicely, and the crowd was
filling in what had been empty spaces on previous visits.

Lisa and I hit the floor immediately, but Rebecca wanted to hang out on the
steps for a while. I'm usually more into acid/techno/trance, but whatever
sub-class was being played there, it really hit the spot! Lisa and I danced
harder and longer than any event since hitting SF, and met some people right there
in the middle of the floor. 

At one point, someone started gyrating against me back-to-back hard and slow.
Turning around, I found a short-haired lesbian girl kissing another short-haired
girl. Blissful confusion incarnate!

I started to worry that Rebecca might be getting bored, but when we made our way
back over to the steps, she had a small crowd of people gathered around the
speaker chatting happily. Since a few people had warned that Wicked's about
dancing, not meeting and talking, this was a real nice surprise!

We stayed and danced till 6:30, then crawled out into the dawn to face the drive
home to 408-land.

I'd definitely go again. I'd even spend another $15. Nice to find yet another
near sure thing in the city!

And, oh, Dave, by the way, the bathroom floor had a facinating mixture of sweat
and urine. I briefly contemplated what it'd be like to lose my footing there, but
only briefly...

take care!
-nate

When I got started, I went to big parties because, well, they were
visible. And with all that crap on the flyer, I'd surely get something
for my $20. And some of the parties were pretty insane, and sometimes
I even got $20 worth.

But it never felt friendly until I went to my first Your Sister's
House, at the recommendation of someone on sfraves. I didn't know
anyone there at all, but when I left I knew 6 people by name, and I
usually don't remember names.

It's difficult to generalize. I've been to big parties that were
friendly (Full Moon in Richmond '93, most C/U and Basics), big parties
that were unfriendly, and all shades in-between. If I go to them, I
try and pick ones I think will be fun in a fun space. Once in a while
I'm terribly wrong, and I kick myself for a month for missing a really
good one that gets rave :) reviews. I've also been to smaller parties
that seemed to be staring contests. You just gotta go and figure out
which specific party turns you on.

There are tried and true parties I *know* are going to suit my vibe,
and they are usually smaller ones. Some of these have been done so
well that I really believe in them and pitch in to help. The smaller
parties usually need all the help they can get :).

I do agree with Ethan on one thing: There's no good reason for any
party to defer to another, as if the other were more righteous. And I
felt this way long before I ever met him.  All parties big or small
have people who need them, and bowing out to another party is to let
those people down. Some people will *only* go to small parties... will
we make them stay home?

One nice thing about F&F is it's only $3, parking is easy, and it gets
a great vibe going early (last time we had a great vibe before the
music even started..). So people can go to both parties! I think it'll
be an awesome night.

Sean

smaller parties usually have a much more positive vibe than larger ones.  
Yeah most people already know each other but that izz a good thing.  I 
find that it's much easier for me to meet others and be open when I'm

did anyone involved in this quickly-getting-old thread ever go 
to a mr.floppy's
party??

floppy's ran against toontown and other big parties almost 
every time it went
off. in its time, it was the equivalent of a good *wicked* 
EVERY time
it went off.  it did not compete, because it did not compare.  
it thrived because a scant few important details never got 
overlooked:
1)venue..the floppy house(jack london club) was beyond compare! 
 2)price..7.00-10.00
3)dj variety-sometimes 8-10 per party-2decks,4decks, 
upstairs,downstairs...
   boggled the mind
4)art..performances,scheduled and improvisional,always a 
sensory treat
5)PSYCHIC-TV !
FNF stands poised on the threshold of becoming a worthy 
successor
to that tradition...a cocoon, of sorts, where the scene 
retreats to undergo 
a self-evaluation/metamorphosis process...crucible ?  ALLthese 
parties this weekend will go OFF ! they don't even bump heads
if you ask me(did you?) EACH is in SUPPORT of the OTHER, get 
it?
(BIG picture, hello?) the energy that will be released and 
shared will give us all
strength...

my advice-save your nickels-try to taste at least 2 of these 
parties on 17 dec
you will expand your understanding of the *vibe* that is at the 
core of this
thing we call raving...you'll also spread more of it..

peace-n-positivity
greg

	Right, so my first legal Wicked came as a birthday present this 
last weekend. Got a ride into SF cuz I got my bag knicked at Down to 
Earth (so I do not have keys to our communal car anymore, nor a driver's 
lisence to show the nice officer) and walked over to the Troc from Market 
(Had forgotten their is a B of A on the corner of Byrant and 5th). Paid, 
and got my hand stamped. And out on to the floor went I...
	Bumped around for a bit and ran into Jovie who decided my whistle 
needed to be in my mouth, but the music at the time did not demand the 
piercing tone of the piece of flourescent orange plastic. Danced, hooted, 
hollered for a bit, but then felt that things were being stagnent. Hmmm, 
Garth was spinning, nice but kinda flat. So up I headed to the chill room 
to find the person I had come with. The chill room was nice, met a 
couple groups of friendly people, one of whom had the most amazing 
feeling hands, I forgot her name though. Taught my little hand thingy to 
a few more people and decided I had become bored...
	So I went back down to dance and that is where I remained until 
somewhere around 7:30 when I stopped to get a drink and was confronted 
with a screaming rapture bearing a relatively lengthy sword (ok, it was 
actually a friend I hadn't seen since the summer and the rapture was made 
of plastic, the sword a meer paper clip. But it does actually scream...)
	The biggest thing I noticed about Wicked (and about Spundae the 
next night) was that people were a hell of a lot ore comfortable with 
themselves then at 18+ parties (I do not mean to reopen this can of 
worms, just an observation). By this I mea those times when eye contact 
is made and then the other person looks way REALLY quickly and every once 
in a while you catch a worried face glancing to see if you are still 
looking in that direction... Which is good cuz I think that when people 
actually make eye contact (and can deal with it, why is eye contact so 
hard to deal with?) the parties tend to be better (hmmm, do I get flamed 
by the lot of the trance lovers?). Right. So Wicked was a good time, both 
for the dance and the talk...

dave

great time, so I'll probably go again. Plus this year we'll get the new
sound system crankin' with no holds barred all nightfor the first time
outside. The spot & production were extremely cool, outdoors, very good visuals,
industrial feeling. All the DJ's pretty much kept more of a harderhouse
/acid/trance feeling through the night (nobody can tear your head apart
quite like these guys, when they try), which matched the spot very well.
This  is one of the reasons that I think they are the top dj's in the city,
they are *very* good at using their music with the location to create a
solid mood.

Hi all,

I am new in this list and this is my first posting. I am a
Dj, Party organizer and Journalist (house music and local
events) in Frankfurt, Germany.
This message is intended for all people who are in any way involved
with a record label or company or who can forward this message
to someone involved. Naturally we have allready quite some 
material but we need now personal contact with the makers and
owners.

Thanks for your help - if someone wants to visit Frankfurt you
know who to ask!

Jens




Markus Weisbeck
Lersnerstrasse 21
60322 Frankfurt am Main / Germany
phone 001149 - 69 - 5969309
Fax/Data 001149 - 69 - 5967132
 
 
 
'Techno/Style' book project
 
We are planning the publication of a book on the subject of 
'Techno/House Design'. We are particularly interested in the 
design of record sleeves, flyers and merchandising (T-shirts, 
baseball caps etc.). We are aware that it will be impossible 
to provide a complete overview, however, we will reflect all 
developments and trends. We intend to include a wide range of 
international work as well as the more well known examples 
of the genre.
 
During our research your label came to our attention. We would 
be most grateful if you could provide us with some information 
about your company and, if possible, examples of your work for 
inclusion in our project.
 
We expect the book to be published in early summer 1995 by a 
respected publishing company specialising in design and in 
particular, books about record sleeves. The publishers are keen 
to ensure that the project will be handled professionally - in 
particular with regards to copyright.
 
About ourselves:
During the last three years both Markus Weisbeck and Martin Pesch 
worked as designer and editor respectively for the cultural 
magazine 'Heaven Sent'.
In 1994 we exibited a selection of influential record sleeves 
throughout the history of pop, together with a sleeve they inspired, 
under the title 'The Retrographic Beat'. The exibition was shown 
in both Frankfurt and Hamburg.
 
 
 
We look forward to hearing from you soon.
 
Yours faithfully
M. Weisbeck/M. Pesch/J.Prewo

prewo@rz.uni-sb.de

On Mon, 12 Dec 1994, Kevin Keiper wrote:

> Isn't it typical?  Just as soon as one person gets a good idea everybody 
> wants to get into the act.  And this is how Ethen must feel.  He was one 
> of the original people who founded the whole house  scene in SF and the 
> night he is about to throw a party that was one of the fore-father's of 
> the whole scene only to have a number of key people, who would still be 
> mucking around doing lame punk shows if it had not been for him (Ethen) 
> plkaying at their first parties.  Now most people would get a knighthood 
> for this but instead all we get are rival parties on hte same night by 
> stealing other people's ideas left right and center.  A scene is not 
> founded on money but on mutual self-respect and it seems to be totally 
> lacking.  In short, Ethen is experiencing the fact that most people 
> involved in the rave scene in sf are a bunch of un-loyal, 
> diss-respectable, money grabbing indidviduals who could not give a fuck 
> about their fellow raver or their fellow promoter/DJ.  People are 
> shitting on you Ethen and that is very slack.
> As far as having more then one major party on the same night this is 
> tricky in a city as small as San Fransisco because people's money is 
> limmited as well as the fact that the music will be the same (or very 
> similer) at all the different parties.  We could get away with having 
> lots of major parties on the same night in London because it is a bigger 
> town, there are lots of different music scenes and people would know taht 
> the music at each of the different parties would be different where as 
> here, because the scene is much more compact, it is far more difficult to 
> do.  I'm not saying that the music or the dj's are better in London (I 
> acctually think that the music here is better then it is in London) but 
> the scene is deffinatly more diverse so it can, therefore, handle many 
> different house scenes which can not really be done.  All the parties 
> happening on that night will be small, under attended affairs and this 
> will not do anyone, any favours and this is sad.  In short, 
> nobody is going to win from this, especially Ethen, and other's 
> (like money grabbing promoter's who have about as much interest and 
> knowledge on the "scene" as the size of their bank ballance) should have 
> more respect for their elders and better's and be safe in the knowledge 
> that your average raver is so musically ignorant that as long as you 
> have lots of flashing lights and eighteen and over door policy you'll 
> pack them in from miles around regaurdless of the fact that they heard 
> all of this music last week.  But then what do I know?
> Yours with deep respect for Ethen,
> Mr.Trippy.
> keiper@itsa.ucsf.edu    
>

To: sfraves@hyperreal.com

  ...In the words of Butthead :)

  The next month is going to be so friggin awesome!  Not only do I have a 
1 month vacation but I have what are potentialy some of the best parties 
of the year each weekend!  If the vibe keeps growing at this rate, 95' is 
going to be amazing! I would just like to make a little list of party 
suggestions for the holidays.  Yes it is a bit biased towards parties the 
parties I know I'll be going to, but... oh well ;)

Dec 17th:

1. Friends and Family - It's going to be crazy!  If PGE could find a way 
to harness the energy at F&F, our power needs would be filled for 
months!  I think the music this time will be the best yet because of the 
wide variety of DJ's in both rooms.  (Hard)Acid, (Hard)Trance, 
(Hard)House (and maybe some stuff too) and (Insane)Ambient.  The price 
can't be beat either.

2. The Gathering - If F&F wasn't happening, there would be now way I 
would miss this.  I enjoy Martin's parties much more then the FTT/Cool 
World's, and always love having tons of lasers and videos and... well... 
Just one MASSIVE environment (sound, lights, people, DJ's etc.)  The 
price is a probably going to be a bit high though, and if you want to get 
high, we're talking about an expensive night out.  If you haven't 
experienced a BIG party in a while, and feel the need... Then do it!

3. Stompy Family and Friends - The DJ's are very nice and the Troc is one 
of my favorite club locations (except the gestapo security) I have a 
feeling the crowd here will be very mixed and if the DJ's do their job, 
it has the potential for being a great night. There are always parties 
each week I don't feel bad for missing, but this is one I would go to if 
it was the only party... OR if it was on Friday! :)

  So, as you can see (at least from my point of view) it doesn't really 
matter what you choose this weekend, it's going to be AWESOME!  A lot of 
people are done with school or are just starting their vacations and will 
have lots of energy to spare. 

Dec 23rd - It's Christmas time.. I don't think I'll be going out, but I 
did see some promising flyers around, and if the energy from this weekend 
carries over It'll be another great weekend... Although it is possible a 
lot of people might take a break to save up for New Years.

New Years! -PARTY SMART!- Don't Fry, Boom, Smoke, Get High, Tweek or Drink 
            and Drive... DMT would probably be a bad thing too :p 

1. Cloud Factory New Year's in Monterey - OK, here is where I am biased :)
if you live in San Jose or Santa Cruz or within a 1-1.5 hour drive of 
Monterey I would LOVE to see you at our party!  We've been putting tons 
of energy into our parties since this summer and have been planning this 
one for a while.  If you want to experience a young, fresh and energetic 
vibe then come check it out.  Plus, when the sun rises you will be in one 
of the most beautiful places in the world, not under some highway :)

2. Wicked Block Party - Not much I can say here.  Will definetly be a 
rockin party just because most of the people who bring Wicked the vibe 
and energy it has will be there, and a lot of 'tourists' will probably 
decide to go to Cool World/FTT.

3. Cool World/FTT - Ack.. When I read "20,000 person capacity" on the 
back of the flyer I got scared. For two reasons: A: With that many 
people, security becomes a problem (take a look at most BIG concerts) and 
seeing anything from a fight to someone just freaking out can be a BIG 
buzz kill. B: For some reason I have a vision that when they do the 
10.9.8.7 countdown 1/3 of the people will be tripping and what know 
what's going on, another 1/3 will be too tough to shout and the other 1/3 
might start cheering but will stop because no one else is... Oh well, I 
could be wrong, but I don't think H-U-G-E parties go over as well in the 
states as they do in Europe (I went to some in London that were 'fucking 
BRILLIANT!')

3. Galen's Party - Sorry, I'm blanking on the name right now :( .. But I 
do know that the Pacific parties (and all the underground posses) always 
have a great vibe at thier parties, and as one of my friends was telling 
me, "It's not the music, it's the vibe.."

Questions you should ask yourself before deciding on a party (or two):

1. Am I going for the vibe? (ie: Wicked often has a very sexual vibe 
while the Pacific parties are very friendly and F&F insane high energy.)

2. Can I afford it? or Do I get what I pay for?

3. Will my friends be there? (Those of us that party a lot usualy know 
which party are other 'rave' friends will go to.  It's always nice to be 
amongst people you know and love and have a great time with!

And that's that... (shameless self promotion coming up ;) I hope all of 
you who plan to go to multiple parties on Saturday will stay at F&F at 
least till 4 (It would be nice if you could stay all night, but trying 
out other parties is healthy) because I've been waiting to spin at F&F 
for almost 6 months and I finally am!
I am also FULLY 1000% PSYCHED to: Wear holes in your 
socks, send you into rave convulsions (aka insane dancing), communicate 
with aliens and take the combined energy of everyone at the party and 
channel it into the mixer! :)

 See you all on Saturday!!!

Peace out and much love and energy!

-Ernie 'DJ Deaks'

I went to floppies foer most of my first parties, I went by toon town and 
it looked like a bunch of drunk yuppies, Floppies did to of course, but I 
felt comfortable there. I must say it was freakish and arty and no one 
ever talked to me but it was fun and wierd. I thought the sound and music 
sucked most of the time but it always had a feeling of being out of control.
It seemed like a large scale spaz with a very diverse crowd.

onse i walked into a room that was all green and a green naked woman on 
green stick furniture and actuall roll turf making it cool and quiet, sod 
absorbed sound. The next room had slabs of meat everywhere. It was acid 
party not eccy.

salutations, allen@ameba

Subject: My theory on "Cloud 9"
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com

First, let me state that the law is pretty clear on selling
either drugs or foods.
If "Cloud 9" is a drug, and is promoted as being psychoactive
and similar to say, MDMA, (an illegal drug) then posession
of any amount of said substance that was promoted as being "similar" to
MDMA would be prosecuted essentially in the same way.
And the weight of the substance would be used to calculate
the penalty in the same way that would be done for the substance that
"Cloud 9" was represented as being similar to..
In other words, possesion of say, one gram of "Cloud 9" would
be considered to be as serious an offense as possesion of one gram of MDMA.

On the other hand, if "Cloud 9" is a food, there is aclear case
of copyright infringement going on.
"Cloud Nine" is a registered trademark of the Cloud Nine candy bar
company, and I doubt if they would take kindly to copyright infringement.

There is also the issue of honesty in packaging.
A food (or drug) manufacturer is required by law to list the ingredients
in their product. There are lots of reasons for this, none the least
of which is the identification of what would be the cause of any adverse
reaction it would cause.. From what I can see..the Cloud Nine
people have not been forthright about their ingredients.

This is wrong.

And if they were anything other than a front for something far more sinister
they would have been busted long ago..

I think that C9 is some kind of a sting operation, or perhaps
a project set up by the FDA or the DEA to make medicinal use of herbs
illegal, something the FDA and the AMA have been trying to do for a long time..

If you want to patronize them, it's your choice..

Regarding these comments:

>>yeah... yeah.. wicked was ok...sorta mebbe awesome.. :)
>>sumptin' missin tho'... dont know what it was...

>Brian, I agree that "sumptin' missin tho'... dont know what it was..."  But
>I think it was lack of good Music....
>What I'm saying is the music sucked after that.  I enjoy good house music
>but this was lame.  Very low music energy.  
                     ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
Yeah, the low energy/low bpm music was the big, however only,
disappointment of my evening. I thought that the last Wicked I attended 5
mos. ago at Townsend totally went off in every way -- even though I'm not
the biggest fan of the DJ's
and their music. In comparison, I thought last Saturday's event, though
having a great vibe, had mostly sucko music on the main floor when I was
there between 1:00 and 4:30. The quality lacked and the bpm was just way
too slow for me. 

I had go to the upper floor/ambient area a couple of times to escape some
really unbearable stuff, the second time after whoever played a Blondie
tune. I know every word to that song, but if I want to hear that I'll go
hear Steve Masters spin it in the Red Room at the Sound Factory.

Upstairs was where I really enjoyed the music!! Though the ecstatic crowd
nd soft seating were missing, I had a much better time dancing to the music
in the upper room than on the main floor.

Of course it was great seeing Amit, Giamma, and the other SF Ravers! And,
I'm really looking forward to the musical excellence and higher bpm's at
F&F!!

Regards,
Rob

Here you go!  It's an early Xmas, and Santa has brought you Friends
and Family, the Gathering, and the Stompy Stomp all on one night.
Friends and Family, of course, is the SFR collective party and has
scored four knockouts already and promises to be great once again;
the Gathering is one of the granddaddies of the SF Rave scene; I met
some of you for the first time at the "final" Gathering when SFR was
in its infancy.  Preston's Stompy Stomp has a good lineup too, 
sooo...have as much fun as you can afford!!!

"Captain, it's the strangest thing! The Borg suddenly are ceasing
all hostilities!"

"Lieutenant Warf, Your analysis please."

"Captain I believe it is a subtle trick on their part"

"No Warf, I sense some strange emminations coming from that small
class M planet in the adjacent system, Data wasn't that planet
settled by a combined betazoid/humanoid contingent about a century ago?"

"Yes councelor you are correct, the "HouseNation Posse" as they, at one
time refered to themselves by, were a renegade group of anarchistic individuals
who were completely devoted to a "unique form of music" which surfaced
on earth in the late 20th early 21 century.  They assign great value to this
music, almost religeous significance. And are completely dedicated to living
in and spreading what they refer to as "The Vibe""

"Vibe? What is this Vibe?"

"Allow me to explain,  During the late 20th century on Earth, a type of 
"millenial feaver" began to surface as the calender approached the year 2001.
A strange phenomena of all night dance parties, often fueled by psychoactive
drugs swept across the industrialized countries of the time."

"Yes! I remember now!  These ecstasy cults spawned some of the most innovative
artist and scientist that Earth ever knew!"

"That is correct councelor, about a century ago a group of young people
from your planet teamed up with another large group from Earth,  together they
formed the HouseNation, they inhabited this small planet, and since then
have been joined by people from many different races and cultures.
There major export is Music, Art and amazing Cybernetic Technology, to
our best knowledge, they have absolutely no forms of sophisticated
weaponey"

"Yet the Borg seem immobilized, what could cause that"

"Yes... I'm getting it now, wait Geordie, can you patch the bridge into
these hailing frequencies..."

"What the devil is that!"

"That Captain, is House Music, in fact I believe it is the part of the
subgendre labled "Acid House".

"But how can simply beaming a strange form of music immobilize the Borg?"

"You see, Warf it's not just the music, it's this energy that they refer to
as the Vibe, when the betazoids and earthlings interbread, they created a
new race that had exceptional psychic powers, not only were they telepathic
but they figured out how to amplify telepathic thought and even emotions
and transmit them over long interstellar distances" 

"You mean mind control!, Turn this music off at once!"

"Wait Warf, not exactly, you see the HouseNation has a doctrine of non
violence, their demigods are historic individuals like Earth's
Ghandi and Martin Luther King, and Beta's Zenna, they don't seek to
control other cultures, but they do believe in the concept of Aggape or
unconditional love, apparently they are hitting the Borg with their 
"secret weapon" a Luv Phaser.

"Luv Phaser?"

"Yes, they have managed to build a device that can amplify and send
emotions out that are so powerful that they have a direct effect on
the life forms that the beams come in contact with."

"But, but the Borg are a cruel heartless race totally incapable of such
emotions!"

"Well Mr. Warf judging from the effect that this Luv Phaser is having
on that Borg ship, it seems that you are mistaken"



I'll see you all on the dancefloor this weekend!!

				G

>SFRaves List Founder Brian Behlendorf To Appear in Club Wired
>+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+--+
>
>For years, San Francisco has nurtured one of the country's thriving
>rave (or house party) scenes. The all-night, underground parties - whose
>philosophy rests on the principles of Peace, Love, Unity and Respect -
>invigorate the city's night life (and decorate its landscape with
>meandering, hat-wearing teenagers who couldn't find the rave). In many
>ways, these sporadic, not-quite-spontaneous underground parties are the
>arrhythmic heartbeat of '90s urban youth culture. But where did they come
>from? What keeps the culture alive and the community thriving? And how do
>you find out about them anyway? If you're a denizen of this nocturnal
>world, or if you've never quite understood why people would stay up all
>night wearing big, silly hats, then check out Cafe Wired this Thursday, and
>groove with our all-star cast: Brian Behlendorf, who founded and maintains
>the SFRaves mailing list; and Nori Castillo, who planned many of SF's
>biggest and best-known house parties, including The Gathering, Toontown,
>Come-Unity, and Mr. Happy's Disco; not to mention Jen Walsh and Natalia
>Anguiano, two of Wired's most active ravers.
>
>
>Thanks for reading, and stay Wired!

Below, you will find directions for buying DJ Tapes by MAIL/On-Line and a
current DJ TAPE INVENTORY LIST from AMEBA.

This is an advertisement, but......

(Me, Robert Johnson, honorary Sfraver, and Christmas Good-Guy, dreamed up
this Holiday Project, and am offering it to all Sfravers in the spirit of
Christmas, and for the benefit of the FRIENDS & FAMILY community-Sfravers,
Ameba, and the Dj's)---End of Disclaimer....
*************************************************

Last week, someone posted a story about making a fast and furious effort to
purchase the new  DORAN tape, only to find AMEBA closed!!!!!!  Like many
people, whether you live in San
Francisco, or are one of the long distance Motorheads (I live in Monterey)
it's not always easy to get to AMEBA to buy Dj tapes. 

After Geoff White's post about shopping at AMEBA for all your
Sfraves Friends & Family this Christmas, I asked if I could purchase Dj tapes
by mail. Their joyful and effusive holiday response was YES!!!! And YOU can
buy tapes this way too!!!!!!!

      So,  Here's the deal..........(Directions)

1.  Contact Ameba@netcom.com for current inventory of Dj     
     Tapes (See attached for AMEBA DJ TAPE INVENTORY 
      LIST)

2.  TAPES are $16.28 each-- (this includes tax)

3.  CHECKS or MONEY ORDERS

4.  (You will Need 2 kinds of Mailing Envelopes)

       Mailing Envelopes AND Pre-Paid Postage Return Mailers

     A.  Costco, or Office Depot etc. have an assortment of
           plain manila envelopes AND the crush resistant air-
           bubble mailers which are great as the RETURN mailer. 
           

5.  After you have purchased MAILERS, selected the TAPES you 
     wish to buy, AND included CHECK or MONEY ORDER, ADDRESS :

              A.  (Outside Manila Envelope) To:

                              AMEBA
                              1732 Haight St.
                              San Francisco, Ca.   94117

               B.  (Inside)--Self Addressed-Prepaid mailer
                                    (Crush Resistant Bubble envelope)

                                    1. Take the number of BLANK TAPES
                                        you are buying with you to the
                                        post office--Have the Postal Clerk 
                                        weigh the  mailer (w/tapes) and put 
                                        postage on RETURN mailer. ( Example:
  
                                        To Monterey, it is 75 cents Return 
                                        Postage for each tape from SF)

Here are some signs and notices written in English that were discover=
ed
throughout the world.  You have to give the writers an
 "E" for Effort...or not.

In a Tokyo hotel:
Is forbidden to steal hotel towels please.  If you are not a person t=
o do
such thing is please not to read notis.

In a Bucharest hotel lobby:
The life is being fixed for the day.  During that time we regret that=
 you
will be unbearable.

In a Leipzig elevator:
Do not enter the lift backwards, and only when lit up.

In a Belgrade hotel elevator:
To move the cabin, push button for wishing floor.  If the cabin shoul=
d
enter more persons, each one should press a number of wishing floor.
Driving is then going alphabetically by national order.

In a Paris hotel elevator:
Please leave your values at the front desk.

In a hotel in Athens:
Visitors are expected to complain at the office between the hours of =
9
and 11 a.m. daily.

In a Yugoslavian hotel:
The flattening of underwear with pleasure is the job of the chamberma=
id.

In a Japanese hotel:
You are invited to take advantage of the chambermaid.

monastery:
You are welcome to visit the cemetery where famous Russian and
Soviet composers, artists, and writers are buried daily except
Thursday.

Not to perambulate the corridors in the hours of repose int he boots =
of
ascension.

n
the form of a finger; roasted duck let loose; beef rashers beaten up =
in

Drop your trousers here for best results.

Dresses for street walking.

Order our summers suit.  Because is big rush we will execute customer=
s
in strict rotation.

I hope that what comes of this is not just a money making bomb.
I would like it if people took this list and added tapes and reviews
so that we may have the kind of reference that is bigger than the efforts 
of one. our inventory is but a small turd compared to the massive amount 
of tapes out there.  I hope that a more global list will emerge , one so 
large that sue happy record company lawyers will think twice about trying 
to defend an out moded form of money making -intellectual property.
I think the ability to create is more valuable than a creation.
So If anyone has an "original thought" on the matter, I am trying to put 
together an article on intellectual property for xlr8r, and would love 
"facts" and "quotables"

I would like to mention that tape sales will never pay our rent but it 
does pay for many of the records you hear when you go out.

If anyone thinks this was a vile act of bad net-tiquette please flame me 
publicly or privately as your taste dictates.
salutations, allen@ameba

Greetings Friends!

Well the hullaballoo seems to be behind us and from what I can tell I think
we'll all be bumping (and grinding hopefully ;) into each other sometime
tomorrow night. Should be one of hell of a night! I look forward to seeing
you all then -- somewhere :)

Before heading off into the great beyond I did however want to share some
great news with you:

The long awaited Komotion ventilation upgrade has been accomplished! Word
is that that there is now a hole in the wall with a fan capable of turning
over 40,000 cubic feet of air a minute! I don't know about you but I'm
actually gonna miss the famed F&F tropical mini-vacation; it gave me such a
good excuse to wear all my favorite boxers :)

I also wanted to specifically invite all of you to participate in the
Friends & Family festivities tomorrow. I think one of the things people
have liked about F&F is that you can pretty much come down and do
*anything* you want. In the past people have brought alters, disco balls,
art projects, friends, family, stuffed giraffes, nude guys, blow pops and
bellydancers. There's plenty of room for you to contribute whatever you'd
like to this party. We also always need volunteers to come and help set up
and clean up which also happens to be a great way to meet the people
involved who, for the most part, are all your net friends from right here:
sfr!

F&F is also a great way to experience the amazing collection of talent
we've got here on sfr. Almost very single particpant in this party, from
djs and musicians, to visual artists, alter artists and other artists --
all are from sfr; by the people and for the people. Right On.

that said,
luv phasers on; engage...

:)

see ya 'all tomorrow
ethan

PS: If you want to come down and help we'll be there from 6pm on; call the
info line (415.985.5244) for exact directions.

Message-Id: <Pine.SUN.3.91.941218152821.23901B-100000@crl2.crl.com>
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

Recently I inhaled a rather distressing rumor involving one of my own 
experiences, and I must now attempt to prevent this untruth from spreading 
further.  Freezer provided electronic ambience in the upstairs room of 
the Halloween episode of Megatripolis, and over a month later I find a 
rumor circulating to the effect that Megatripolis did not pay us - this 
offered as evidence of the promoters' business practices.  As always with 
rumors, the truth resembles the tale, but only in part.  At the end of a 
long night and an even longer morning, I prepared to leave the party and 
began to look around for a familiar face connected with the event, in 
order to inquire after any money that may or may not have been left for 
the musicians and DJs in the upstairs room.  Finding no familiar faces 
and being at that point more desirous of sleep than of money - of which I 
had not really been expecting much - I went home.  If Freezer and our 
many collaborators of that evening were not paid, this was the result not 
of the promoters' stinginess but rather of our own lack of effort in 
obtaining payment.  In fact, we found that the Megatripolis crew were 
quite a pleasure to work with, and we were quite pleased that they showed 
such support of the local electronic musi-community in allowing us free 
reign of the upstairs all night.  Neither we nor the other players in the 
upstairs room were after money that evening anyway - we were quite happy 
just to get so many keyboards and drum machines hooked into the same 
sound system and play our sets in a large space to an appreciative 
crowd.  This brings me to the soapbox section of the message:  (1) rumors 
blow around endlessly in our little scene and should be greeted with 
distrust; (2) rumors grow around a kernel of truth which evolves into 
falsehood through repetition and distance; (3) rumors serve to spread 
only confusion, often damaging their subjects and their tellers.  I have 
heard many tales about various promoters and musicians in the scene, 
which stories, upon closer scrutiny, start looking a bit fishy.  One 
person might tell a tale of an interaction with X, and the listener, 
honestly misunderstanding, might then repeat a slightly modified version, 
which then evolves into an inaccurate rumor.  Stories should be checked 
for accuracy before they are offered as nonfiction.  Yes, there are 
predators hovering over the scene - psychic predators, cultural predators, 
financial predators - but we need to make sure of their indentities 
before we go telling tales.  The Megatripolitans put on some nice parties 
with excellent music and low prices, so we should not be directing the 
dark energy of rumor and untruth their way.  Sorry for the soap suds.  
:)  Joshua / Freezer

Ahhh!  My head is still spinning sweetly from such a glorious night!
I got there at about 11:30 and the place was already hopping.  I wish I 
didn't miss Doran's set, but the other dj's made up for it big time.
Spun made his usual grand entrnace, I didn't even have to be at the turn 
tables to see that it was him coming on:)   Tony, as always, just blew me 
away, and I heard some of John Williams' set which was really fast and 
hard core, (and quite good, rather mesmerising) but after dancing for 
several hours, I was ready to chill for 
awhile in the ambient room.  I met up with Jason Sydes from sfraves and 
we and his friend, Gwen kicked back. Soon we had a bunch of people joining 
us; some who I hadn't met before (Ian, Christa, & Ryan) and some who I 
knew, but not very well: one you all know, Tony Garcia (deepfog).  I 
found a deeper plane of friendship in him that night.
After a couple of hours (I think.....length of time is difficult to 
comprehend at a great rave) Tony and I hit the dance floor again and Josh 
was on playing some really upbeat morning music.  I couldn't stop 
dancing!  I've always like the acid trance stuff the best.....but Josh 
and Garth's sets (ESPECIALLY Garth) made me appreciate morning music in a 
whole new way.  From Josh's set til the music stopped, I was held captive 
on the dance floor never once standing still.   When Garth was on and 
that song that was playing when the lights last came on (it was, I was 
told a sort of disco song where they were singing "it's so real")  
Anyway, the vibe was so strong and INTO it and that song.........it just 
literally brought me to tears!! So I was there grinning like a fool, 
dancing like a crazy, and tears streaming down my cheeks! It was bliss!
(I'm getting goosebumps again as I type:)
After the music stopped, I met 2 more people from sfraves: phuture and 
Josh Bates.  I can't wait to meet you guys again soon and actually get to 
talk.       I hope I haven't taken up too much room, just so much to 
tell-you know how it goes. If Friends & Family and Stompy Stomp went off 
like the Gathering, it's a wonder that the whole bay area didn't blast 
off to the moon!!!  
Talk to you all soon,
luv,
Amy

 Friends & Family & Friends .....

 After a day of holiday shopping , I started my evening by stopping at
Kommotion to help set-up. With the efforts of us all , the music was
playing by 9:15PM. I decided to bug out and check on Stompy Stomp at
the Trocedero , but not before I hand-painted a day-glo heart on one
of the wall-mounted sheets of paper. As I was leaving , Gil and the
Normals  arrived to set up their ambient U-Haul! A great idea - for $20,
a truck can be rented for 24hrs. that can serve as an exterior chill space.

 I found a nice parking space about 30 yards from the Trocedero - as
I was early , I took a nap. Refreshed , I walked up to the door to
find out that it was still closed at 10:10PM . The door guy says "open
in 15 minutes". So , I decide to "CHILL" outside , since the doors
would be open soon. Luckily , DJ Harry Who came by with his box o'
vinyl - he managed to get me in early as a guest. 

 It turned out that doors didn't officially open until 10:50 PM , 50 
minutes after the time on the flyer. Nagging technical problems were
to blame for the Stompy family's delay. 

 The first thing I noticed was the wall-of-sound speaker setup - ten
feet wide and eight feet tall , each wall composed of eight Eastern
Acoustic Works (EAW) speakers , one wall on each side of the turntable
platform. This platorm was unique - suspended at the four corners by
doubled 1/8" cables , reinforced by 2x4s at each end nailed to the 
edge of the stage. No connection to the dancefloor. This was done to 
avoid the vibrations from the floor.

 The system sounded OK to me - I did notice during the night that the
sound did change somewhat depending on location and crowd density , but 
since there was no trouble to move to any part of the club , it was 
no bother. The sound was never distorted - just some bass "tubbiness"
in some spots.

 Harry Who started the night off , so his was the set with the lowest 
audience. Too bad - he did a nice mix of stuff that I had fun dancing to.
During his set , I took a break and checked out the upstairs. They were
still setting up - lotsa bean bag chairs , hip-hop , but no sushi. 

 By the time I left at about 12:30 AM , during John Howard's set. By 
that time , the attendence had increased to about 15 people. A special
Stompy dancer was doing a go-go thing on the big platform - her costume
was a sort of ballerina bird woman with silver beak , silver skirt , and
wispy wings. 

 Back to Friends and Family - SHEESH! It was the most crowded I had
ever seen for a Kommotion F&F event. Shortly after I got there , the
door checker and Bryce had to stop people from coming in. People every-
where. I tried dancing in the crowd , but gave it up after about half
an hour. After milling about some , I escaped to the ambient U-Haul 
truck.

 Seems most of the ambient truckers were SFRavers I know - maybe the 
rest of the crowd didn't know that the truck was "public access"? It was
nice to be in a quieter space - on my second bean bag chair of the night.

 Looked like Friends and Family didn't need my attendence to help with
the great and humid vibe , so I decided to head back to the Troc , which
was underattended when I left. I

 Boy - they didn't need my help either! By this time , Doc Martin was
spinning , and the crowd had increased to about 1.5 times the Friends
and Family crowd! Density was about 9 square feet of dancing area per
person , as opposed to F&F density of about 6.5 square feet per person.
It was a joy to have the additional floor space to do some elbow-jab
free dancing. I saw other "refugees" from F&F - that white haired
couple ( what's their name? do they have a daughter/granddaughter who
raves? ) , Robert , and Derek Chung. 

 The Stompy crowd was in good spirits - no lack of vibe on the dance
floor! I'll have to remember to catch Doc Martin again - I liked a
heck of a lot of what I danced to. The crowd certainly enjoyed his
set , and let him know so vocally.

 More Stompy dancers in different costumes, don't remember the costume
details very well. Upstairs was being fully utilized chill-wise , the
music still hip-hop and trip-hop.   Still no sushi.

 I decided to call it a night at 3:30AM ... as I drove southwards , I
was glad to know that both parties had succeed , attendence-wise. I hope
that they ended OK ( but that's for other folks to report on ...).

 [ Glad to see Frank and "Jump In The Fire" again - long time no see!]
 
        Larry Ching / larryc@netcom.com

To sum things up _This party WENT OFF!_

I arrived around 7:30 to set up my equipment and sound check. The party 
pretty much started then as Ernie,Phred , Ethan and myself played some 
tracks to warm up the old SoundVision system and music was going and 
people were decorating in the ambient room.

It was crowded but the heat wasn't too bad and there was a real nice 
mix of people. There was still a decent size group of diehards when I 
came on at 6am to close things down. The sound was excellent and my ears 
were not ringing even after DJing (that is a very good sign). It was great 
to see so many familiar faces, Lee & Janie Fogel, Giamma & Maura, Gil, 
Ernie,Phred, Joe, Morgan, Tamara & everyone else. Extra special thanx to 
Ethan & Bryce :)

For those few music lovers who made it through my set here's the set list.
It was a blast , can't wait to the next one. Hope to see you all at 
_Begin Again_ on New Year's.

Ronan

anticipation of tip income..(which they do make with the nightclub crowd..)

tips.. but only $50.00 if there weren't decent tips...typically..

Ann queries:
>ps what's up with the full moon thing?

Well, as I walked out of Komotion to evaporate some love drops of sweat, in
the late am fog, I saw a shy, sultry moon dance low over the horizon, ready
to give the sky back to the sun. And walking back in, I knew this had been
my full moon. Deaks set had peaked my night, and I imagined hearing him
again on a beach in Monterey, blowing my bubbles over a happy crowd, and as
my starry eyes cleared, Bryce showed up in the foreground, grinning at two
young, experienced ravers, and said  "well, tonight WAS the Full Moon, and
we've been celebrating it and ourselves tonight" or something pretty damn
close, if happy memory serves.

There's part of your answer, girl! The rest, well, after an hour more of
work, I'll spill mah beans!

Lotsa love,
 Milton and the "Oh, so satisfied" E-Bee..........

Wow. Friends & Family was totally *nuts*; sick, sick, sick, sick! +)
Jam packed and bubbling with just psycho vibe.

Music was phenomenal all night. With a few notable exceptions, the lineup
in both rooms was composed almost entirely of *unknowns* and lemme tell
you, they all went crazy. Jamie's opening set in the chill room was prolly
the best chill set I've ever heard. Soul, R&B, Motown, Funk & House all
rolled into one, truly great! Gil, Jeyson, Lee, Ernie, Phred, Ronan, WBL,
Freezer, Brian and Laura, Joe Rice, Mohsen and Michael; all were fantastic!

Visuals were out of this world: two screens of meclay madness, wonderful
real time graffiti, wall hangings, posters, suns, moons, stars, oil
projections... :)   :)

Many, many thanks to *everyone* that helped in making this one go so off.
There are way too many of you to mention without forgetting someone; you
know who are :) Extra, extra special thanks to our pre- and post-clean up
crews. The place looked (and smelled) wonderful! And coiling cables by dawn
in the tropical komotion mud requires a truly special breed of person;
thank you all!

Also to Komotion who really stretched their boundaries for us on this one.
The enire joint was fully packed with a huge line outside most of whom,
unfortunately, were unable to get in. Definitely our biggest party yet. If
you can't get flattened by the 3 year gathering and a stompy stomp, I think
you're there :) Glad to hear, however, that all three went so totally off.
Does SF rule or what? ;)

see ya next time
ethan

...whatever that means.

So: after a long absence involving the release of my arcade game, a
month-long odyssey across the US on a bright red motorcycle, a
$100,000 lawsuit, and some other stuff, I finally had my chance to
dance.  After Saturday, I have several questions:

1) Deaks, man: you blew up!  Where'd all that come from?  Woke me up from
sleeping behind the piano!

2) Will the Glowing Mouth become the new trend in all-night energy boosters?
Bonus: it's hard to project a 'tude when your lips are fluorescent green.

3) Just where _did_ Milton get that hat?

4) What happened to that huge five-foot fan that Komotion used to have?
I know I missed it.

5) Is it my imagination, or has the F&F hug quotient increased over its
last few incarnations?

6) Why did I have to miss so many of these?  Damn.

It's great to be back.  Thanks to everyone for being there: if I tried to
name everyone I'd go nuts.  You know who you are.

...and in case anyone wonders, I was the tall guy in biker shorts with the 
long ponytail and the Van Dyke -- and occasionally the tiger shirt and 
bubble kazoo.

// g

I guess the upshot of bobbo's story is that Megatripolis promised payment
for his performance and didn't deliver.  Whether or not you stick around
to receive your compensation, it seems to me that the requestor of the
service ought to get in touch with the provider and set things straight
one way or the other.

In this scene, making money is not the primary motivator of many of the
people involved.  But it's still important for the integrity of the
house/techno/rave scene overall that obligations are satisfied and that
those who do want to make money don't take advantage of those who do not.



Just my $0.02 (discounted commercial rate) . . .

phred

What a great party!  And after a lot of agonizing over my first set for
any large group, I felt pretty good about it.  Deaks wrecked my strategy
by *ripping* it up in his set, so I couldn't go with Plan A (spacey trancey)
or Plan B (tribal funky) so it was Plan C after all (details below).

Well, knowing that the Groove Kitchens
don't get going very early I went by a suburban
early eighties metal theme party (nicely done)
to chomp on mini-corndogs and play silly
drinking games (Coors Light, of course)

I suppose a party like that seems charming if
(1) you've been to real ones (2) it's been quite
a long time since you've been to a real one.  ;-)
Anyway, I'm kinda into dramatic contrasty evenings, it 
makes a city nightclub all the more fabulous, full immersion
then brings on some of that overwhelming innocent awe ...

Off to Stompy we go - there were no lines around 2 and
the party was Cookin - I love walkin into a Hotbox Frenzy!
They made the Troc a little cozier than I've seen before with 
the stage being occupied by a big screen; the speakers and dj table 
were kinda sticking out onto the dance floor, and this great dancer
platform/cage-like thing was smack in the middle of everybody.
I liked the more intimate atmosphere.

The dancers and costumes were fantastic.
The first one I saw was the Angel Bird Lady
who was just Frozen into the most inspirational
graceful pose.  She was Flyin ...  there were several
dancers and they each did multiple costume changes.  
They took live video of em and spiced up the
otherwise ho hum ravey visuals on screen.

I caught the last of John Howard (burnin off that Coors Light)
and was pretty loose for Doc Martin.  He played for about 4 hours
which presumably gave me a good intro to his stuff and I think he
worked up into a nice groove.  It was all good.  Freestyle, richer
sounding House?  There were lots of rythm changes and the music
would abrubtly vary itself - wild at times.  The sound was
good - not everywhere, but you could certainly find
places with room to move and your level volume.

The crowd was friendly and definitely Older.
Lotsa very cute folks, lotsa dancing, lotsa playful cynicism.
It was very loose and sloppy.  This was partly the music, I guess,
but I noticed a whole bunch of down right silliness.  It was hard
not to dance in a super-goof splashy manner.

Love ya,
Dave

As always, it went OFF and it just seems to keep getting better!!  I had to 
leave around 4, in preparation for a drive to Santa Barbara, but things were
ragin' and bumpin' and I could barely tear myself away to go!

I brought along a "rave virgin" friend and I think he's hooked.  He can't
wait until the next one either.  :)  Thanks to everyone who made it happen,
I'm just always so amazed at how great everything always turns out, and the
amazing vibe we're able to create!  I got so many hugs and met so many
wonderful sfravers and non-sfravers alike (you know who you are!) that even
though I was sick as a dog I still felt great.  :)  I even got smiles and
hugs from some gangsta types who were sorta glaring around - it's amazing
what a little jolly rancher and a big smile will do.  :)

who contributed to the great vibe, especially the dj's and everyone I got a big

F&F was killer.  I even managed to stay awake until 5:30, which is a
recent record for me.  I danced so hard to Ethan's set and to the bits
of acid at the end of Ernie's that I pulled a muscle in my leg.  You should
see me limp :-( .  Man, when I was in the back of the main room with
MikeBee, Steve B., Ovid, and everyone else whooping and screaming along
with the squaking aceeeeid noises I felt that special energy and excitement
that I'd just been too tired and cynical to feel lately.

It's amazing what havok we (all of us together) have wrought.  Stay tuned
for a great '95!

John (jump in the fire) steps on hot coals:
>2) Will the Glowing Mouth become the new trend in all-night energy boosters?
>Bonus: it's hard to project a 'tude when your lips are fluorescent green.

 Hmm! That's right! You do make people smile at you, even if you don't, if
yer teeth and lips glow. I think this may be a new tool to disarm 'tooders
and cruisers! 
 If anyone noticed, there were 5 or 6 guys in from the mission (yes, I am
going by appearance/accent, but I am latino so shut up) that may have just
stumbled  upon the line outside by accident and decided to check it out,
hey it's 3 bucks, right?
 And they were on those stairs, kinda watching the party and bobbing their
heads, but kinda drawn back. Defensive, you know, the railing as a barrier
and safety in close numbers! But they laughed at me and I let them know it
was ok to do that. They wanted some E, but of course, this ain't yer
buyer's market. But not to let them down, I gave them some rue. 
 And then it happened. They came off the stairs, danced, and my anonymous
friend(you know who you are) saw one of them, green lips and all, TRANCE
OUT and lock into the rythm and spiral off into that other world. 
 Makes me really warm and even a little smug when that happens, that
someone can stumble across this and the vibe be so strong it draws them in,
and they fit right in after a while. Hope their next party is a good one,
too.
Maybe in a few more parties, they might come back in drag with me. And hit
up on the security at the troc "hey, big boy! Is that a mag-light, or are
you just happy to see me?"

Lotsa love,
 Milton and the E-Bee.....

On Tue, 20 Dec 1994, David Alga wrote:
> > Is the real KLF really playing on New Year's?
> > Is Bill Drummond going to be there?
> > Inquiring minds want to know.
> > It would be pretty intense if they are and he is.
> >         JC
> 
> Yes, that really is KLF performing at Cool World on New Year's.  It's
> their first appearance in the Bay Area EVER.  They're on at 11:30,
> and are bringing on the New Year.  DON'T miss em...  I can't wait.

No, it is *not*.  It is the "KLF Experience featuring Wanda Dee", which 
means a former backup singer crooning over tapes of KLF music without 
Drummond or Cauty's permission at all.  You might as well have "The 
Velvet Underground Experience featuring Nico" with Nico singing over some 
old VU albums.  Drummond and Cauty have not performed as the KLF in over 
two years, and they don't have the money to fight a legal fight against 
Wanda Dee and her record label over the copyright infringement involved 
here.  

	Brian

Oh mah gawd! Relax people!
 Let's thank cool world for providing a place for those with tastes
different from most of us on sfraves and most of those we meet at parties.
I'm sure anyone who identifies with the  CW flier and both the obvious and
subliminal info on it ("intelligent lighting") will enjoy their party. It
is $20, all of us have paid that for a new years wicked or a Martin party,
many of us have been to FTT (and they are there on Alga's boat). 
 Yes, it's commercial. It's a little on the velveeta side. And there IS
mind fucking on the flier (klf experience!hmpf!). I for one will not go to
an event that insanely huge even to see Zeus display his lightning
collection, if I have to put up with the rest of the crap. But that's my
taste. Most people going there don't know KLF, don't care, will be in
another"arena" or will be so whacked they won't even care. Or they just
wanna rock and their friends are there.

Lots of them will be happy at the end.
Lots will have new friends. 
Lots will have puked out that chilli they sell there.

But if he's still in business, that means he's got a market.  Good for him.
But Dave, you gotta level at least with us. Don't try to smoke us; and
people, don't say "go to wicked, that's a real rave." Cow palace security
is kinder, gentler, than what wicked and DV8 will have hired.DV8 porta
potties will have hundreds of people puking bunk e, hordes of kids will be
against the wall freakin on three hits of lucy, and the big, angry samoan
will be looking for my ass.
 But my ass is gonna be at the Pacific party, or "down" in Monetery/SC at
the cloud factory. New years is gonna rock for everyone, everwhere. Depends
on why you do what you do.
 Think about it, sugars.

Lotsa love,
 Milton and the E-Bee....

Ok since I was there and I haven't posted in a while(work,work,work)
Killer sound, massive stacks that just slowly lure you closer and closer.
 Pounding and clean.
John Williams spun an incredible high speed hardcore set(isn't he usually
slow and funky?). It worked for me better than any other hardcore set I've
heard recently.  I think I hurt myself though...
I'm not sure where I was during Josh's set but I liked it.
Garth can really rip it up(like we don't know THAT) I think he must've had
the echo cranked all the way on I I Feefeeel Luuuuuluuuluulove but it was
truly brilliant in timing, feel and groove.  I could  feel massive waves of
love/vibe flowing outwards through the crowd and right through my body/mind.
You gotta wonder if there were special nights in those old disco years when
everything clicked and they acheived escape velocity. Hi deepfog and I
finally met Amy.
And I'm in love with Mickey Mouse and that angel(seriously, she had these
incredible 4 foot long wings, feathery platform shoes, and short shorts. How
do they know I dreamed that just the other night?)
See ya out there,
phuture

If there are any of rules travel, they are the following:
	Theorem: Never look at your hands.
	Corollary: Never stare at your face in the mirror.

Follow these rules, and you will have many happy trips.

yourself, and look at it the next day. I mean, you didn't think the
faces appearing in the walls and the weird melting and blooming
graffitti in the bathroom were real, did you? Pay no attention to the
man (or woman) behind the curtain!

In lieu of a Christmas Card, I give you this message about friendship in
the harshest of realities.  As you read it, consider that the "I" and the
"You" in the story are layered deep.  They represent our friendship, and
every friendship you and I have ever had.  "I" and "You" are also like
looking at a wire frame box when your eye can't decide whether its looking
at the bottom or the top of the box and the percieved orientation keeps
shifting with every thought.  At the same time, " I" is definitively me,
and "You" is definitively you because how would I have known anything about
friendship if I had never met you? Enjoy.

The Bus Ride
By Purple Tiger
Dedicated to the public domain and ravers everywhere.

With Christmas rapidly approaching, I find myself wanting to share with
you, as my closest of friends, my contentment and satisfaction with the
human race.  I didn't always feel this way.   There was a time in my life
where it seemed that I was strapped immobile to the seat of a school bus
traveling faster than comprehension towards the only brick wall in a
million miles of featureless asphalt.  You were screaming, I was screaming,
we all were screaming but bus driver didn't care.  He was mesmerized, it
seemed, by the brick wall on the horizon and the promise of a final
destination.

I can't even say that I remembered getting on the bus.  Somewhere,
impressed in a history of chemical modulations, is a vague memory of my
parents helping me onto the bus with a ticket stamped "HAPPY BIRTHDAY."   I
can't blame Mom and Dad that much, the atmosphere was a little thick that
day and the brick wall was just a fuzzy jag on the horizon.  It's hard to
be afraid of a fuzzy jag.

I got tired of screaming after a while, and, as you sat in the seat next to
me, you seemed to too.  We broke out the Alphabet Yatzee game and played a
few rounds.  Inevitably words like "NUCLEAR WINTER" and "BIOSPHERE
DESTRUCTION" rolled onto the board a few times, but they didn't seem to be
any different than the other words, except that we never tried to tally the
points on the letters and we were quick to throw them back into the cup.
When we first started, we used to say the words as they came up.  Then one
day you said the word "SPECIES EXTINCTION" and even before the word
finished you started to cry.  The sorrow almost killed you then.  In our
ignorance we didn't know that a spoken word could carry so much power.  I
turned away from you then because I couldn't stand to see you in pain, and
to hide my shame because I was glad it was you who discovered this horrible
truth, and not me.  We stopped saying the words then, and used only the
board to play the game.  That was when we noticed that the rest of the bus
had already discovered for themselves the difficulty of speech, and with
the final silence of our voices, the only sound left was click clack of the
game and the whoosh of the road.  That was when it became my turn to cry.

As the trip wore on (do you remember when we naively called it a journey?),
and the wall got closer, it got easier to keep one eye on the window and
one eye on the game board.   We lived a strange duality then, half of
ourselves transfixed by the approaching wall and the other half playing the
game.  If one ignored the fact that we never faced each other and only half
our faces were smiling, the ride took on the seeming of a normal bus ride.
Even now I can look on that time and say I was truly half-happy, and glad
to have someone to play the game with.  It was better than the alternative.
Do you remember the man in the next row with both eyes forward and a smile
like a bus driver on his face?  I remember when I almost became like that
man, but before I could completely fade away, you slapped me and screamed,
"Don't Leave Me!" to bring me back.  It was also the only time you touched
me, and the only words you've ever said to me.  I will cherish that moment
forever.

I can't say when it happened, but I do know when I noticed.  I remember
when the brick wall slid slightly away from the crack in the windshield.  I
often used the crack as a reference for locating the wall against the
horizon.  At first I thought that the glass had distorted slightly from the
heat of our passage and lamented the loss of a previously dependable site.
With no other landmarks to use as a reference, it was the only thing I
could believe.  As time passed it became clear that no distortion in the
view could account for the ever increasing change.  About that time, my
other eye noticed a slight change in the corded muscles of your neck and a
subtle slowing in your labored breath.  I feared you were sick and started
to worry.  It is with amusement now as I realize that you were only
starting to relax.  Your body had started to hope even before your mind
knew there was a reason.

It feels so different now.  Today I saw the bus driver take his first
breath since I started this ride and his pallor is starting to redden
slightly.  I believe these are good signs.  Blinking can't be far away for
him, I'm sure of it.  I also saw both your eyes for the first time today,
no brick wall, no game board, just your eyes.  We couldn't look long
because the moment was too intense for the both of us.  We haven't spoken
yet because our mouths are still thick with decades of disuse.   We can
hear words being spoken in the back of the bus, but the riders in the back
haven't been on the bus as long as you or me.  Still I'm in no hurry, the
words will come soon.

One of the riders in the back is talking about a party when we drive past
the wall.   Can you imagine?  A party?  We might even get to meet the man
in the next row, or exchange words with the bus driver.  So, will you dance
with me as the red brick wall passes and doppler shifts even redder in the
rear view window?  Will you stand with me as we stare at the ever bluer
horizon in front of us?  Will you hold my hand as we journey into a future
we want to remember?  Do you want to hear me say the words that I've been
throwing onto the board?  Do you?

"I" "Love" "You" "My" "Friend"
"Merry" "Christmas"

--
< Purple Tiger (ptiger@crl.com) >
                  Don't let a chromosome determine your gender.

From: jocelyn@hal.com (Jocelyn Cordell)
Message-Id: <9412222352.AA12834@dre.hal.com>
To: sfraves@hyperreal.com
Subject: review of the spot
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

well, despite health considerations- i made it to the spot last night:
it was wonderful! and certainly has won my own sfraves stamp 
of approval: be forwarned though: a rave it was not. a fantastic 
mixture of location, atmosphere, people and music it was! 

i arrived at 10:30- the first thing you see upon entering the door 
and turning toward the really nice door woman is the bar (ok, to many 
this will seem negative, but please hold them horses) i've lost my id 
and 'til the new one arrives in the mail-
i'm dependent on an old, torn photo driver's license from Texas 
that expired in `88, coupled with my temp driv. lics. with no photo,
and, failing that, la piece de resistance- my work badge- when I 
began to explain, the door woman smiled, waved my papers away and
said, "I trust you." Thanks! I gave her my $3, she gave me a 
drink ticket (yep- your first drink, whatever it is, is on the house-
no limitations, but i talked to the owners and they said they were only 
going to do this once or twice more). Some friends were standing/
seated near the bar, so I went up to say hi, then turned away from 
the bar to take in the place: neat-o! it basically looks like 
two rooms put together with the major dividing factor being 
an enormous, circular, open fireplace/firepit. this scored
major ambience points with me for several reasons: lighting, what 
better than fire, eh? ventilation- not a smokey fire- the flu must
be in proper working order! warmth- this was the first time in a 
long time that i took my jacket off before hitting the dancefloor,
and left it off for most of the evening. 
other stuff i saw: flashing colored christmas lights strewn about 
in a haphazard fashion, interesting, chatty crowd, few dancers (but 
this changed in time). i walked into Mei Lwun's set: he played 
a nice funky acid jazzish set- too bad folks weren't quite up to 
dancing yet- part of the non-dancing thing was created by this 
tapestry that manny had hung up that blocked the one room 
where the DJ was from the room where the bar was- once this was
torn down (by manny, shortly after Mei Lwun's set) dancing started 
to pick up. Mei Lwun was followed by Robert Rankin': he's a 
reggae DJ from Santa Cruz (i think that's where he's from?)- he 
played a great set and started me dancing. Many more joined in the dance 
about 2/3rds of the way through his set. Robert's a really great guy-
you should go to the next one just to meet him, if nothing else. 

Robert was followed by Gravy (i think?): i've never heard/seen him 
before to my knowledge- he played a fun hip hop set that 
set fire to the dancefloor- really got people moving. Since 
I had danced for most of Robert's set, I took a short break to 
rest my feet and get a coke. while at the bar, a couple of 
swingers tried to pick me up! What fun to be so wanted! Did 
I taunt? did I tease? I swear it must be my new shoes. the last time 
i wore them in tower records video department, somebody else 
tried to pick me up- seeing as our first chat was abpout the movie 
bitter moon, it's probably just as well that i didn't take him up 
on his offer ;) anyway, folks, that's what was really great about 
the place- the crowd- a great mix of people who really hung 
in there with a very friendly air throughout the moves from 
acid jazz to reggae to hiphop. very open, very friendly, lots of 
introductions all around. and if the gangstas were in the house, 
you wouldn't have known it from their attitude. also, the staff 
were some of the friendliest i've met in a looong time; and that 
despite the fact that people were passing back drink tickets to 
the bar most of the night and not tipping to boot!

i returned to dance to more of gravy's set, at which point, as
i was walking toward the floor, my friend turned to me and said,
"this is live." and then i noticed that toward the dj table, 
obscured by dancers, there was a group of people passing the mic 
and improvising rap to the dj's mix. Right on! 

I danced a bit more, said my adioses, and exited stage left 
around 1:40. definitely a worthwhile adventure: the spot, every other
wednesday, making the next one jan.4, 1995, $3 (includes one free drink), 
21+, robert rankin' will play again- don't know who else; 502 Auzerais
Ave. in SJ. Come prepared for mellow, chatty warmth.

p.s. Niels, you shouldn't miss the next one if you like the 
stuff that Robert plays- the only other venue he graces is
Ajax, and I have NEVER seen anyone dance there!

just a thought - i live in western australia, which is on the western 
side of australia.  if you find a map of the world you will see that 
australia has 8 different states and territories including tasmania which 
is a smaller island off the southcoast of eastern australia.  New 
Zealand is across from the south eastern coast of australia is actually 
composed of 2 isalnds which are not part of australia!  

as i have not yet been to N.Z. (new zealand) i do not know what their 
party and rave scene is like.

In australia, the best places for the rave scene is Sydney, Melbourne and 
of course Perth (which is where i am).  

if you would like to know any more about oz or about anything at all 
please e-mail me.  my mailbox will be out for about 1 week so between the 
25 December and 3 January i won't be able to reply.

Stay cool, keep raving, be happ-eee.

Work has made it tough for going out mid week, but friday was that
day where everyone brings their kids in for the yearly parental 
dote fest, so I decided to telecommute (i.e. take the day off).
I wasn't really gonna go out thursday, but I called the Pure Space 
line.  Not only was it going to be at 1015 Folsom, one of my all time
favorite indoor venues, but it was going to go until "at least
5:30".  The last time I was at 1015 F. was months ago at a Come/Unity
when the police shut it down and confiscated the mixing board at 3am,
15 minutes into Jeno's set.

It was great to be back.  Spun was spinning a typically trippy and
erratic set when I got there, but with some truly inspiring segments.
The sound was great, deep rich bass, very loud, no distortion.  There
was a screen on the stage with your standard slide projector/video
visuals.  Unfortunately, they didn't use the house lights much, just
some strobes.  There were beanbag chairs and soft benches all over the
place, and the upstairs was open with some chairs and table.  It was
very comfortable.  There was also plenty of free water.  It never got
packed, but the vibe was thick and friendly with plenty of energy to
go around.  Not too many SFRavers that I knew; Geoff, Roxanne, David,
Grey.  I bumped into Galen who was doing some low key selective
flyering for Begin Again.  I don't want to give too much away, but
this party will definately be a rave, and there will be a map point
for the site.  This is not going to be a "100% bust free" event, but
Galen assured me that they have a lot of strategies for dealing with
the police.

Anyway, Markie took over and took me into high orbit with a fantastic
high energy trance-funk set; That alone was more than worth the $5.
Jeno followed with a good set as well.  The party ended at 5:30 with
my legs aching.  I had danced for 4.5 hours, and crawled away very
fulfilled.  Hmm, I wonder if the next Come/Unity there will go all nite
as well?  I might have to start telecommuting more. :-)

Lee
____________________________________________________________________________
lxfogel@pacbell.com   (    (   (  ( ((0)) )  )   )    )    lee@hyperreal.com

you stare into your eyes 3 minutes (listening to plastic man helps!) and
you will hypnotize yourself into seeing yourself as a soul using this body
as a shell. See how your head can turn, but your eyes in the mirror stay
fixed in space. The body rotates around them, and they become tools of your
brain, and that is only a tool for your soul, a connection to this
physicaly biased world. That's all you are, a beautiful shell to protect,
carry and MOVE your even more marvelous  soul.

And then you will really love your friends even more, you will know they
are much more than what you see smiling back at you, they are all
butterflies in the same beautiful sky as you. And they will always be with
you.

Try it! It's my favorite part of "coming down"

A note from The Huge Evergrowing Pulsating
Train Which Travels The ExpressWay To Yr Skull:
 
In the early days of Spring 1995, we will be putting on a FREE outdoor
event consisting mainly of ambient, trance, and experimental soundscape,
on a site in the Angeles mountains on the north side of the Los Angeles
basin.
 
Our motive is to create a sketch-free environment where people can chill
out all night and be exposed to new music and sounds.  There will be
a main area where the music will flow from trance to ambient to experimental
to tribal and back, and another chill-out space exclusively for ambient
and noise (non-traditional IntelliDansMusik).  We will also have poetry
readings, drumming circles, and screenings of obscure cult films.
 
We are currently looking for techno/ambient/electronica musicians and 
DJs who will be in the Los Angeles area mid-March and would be willing 
to volunteer their time and talent to help this event go off.
 
Anyone else who wishes to contribute in the way of performances, lights,
readings, sound, advice, and sheer inspiration, please feel free to contact
the Milk.Weed.Project through PAUL.GERONCA@SUPPORT.COM.
 
As for everyone else, more information will be presented as it is confirmed.

               details to follow.

On Sat, 24 Dec 1994, David Alga wrote:
> What is going on with Hyperreal?  I haven't gotten any mail on the
> list, and the ftp site is down too.  If anyone knows, let me know
> what's up...

The InterNIC got hyperreal.com's DNS record messed up (due to a 
combination of a stupid procedure policy on their part and a mistake on 
someone's domain registration form) and it reverted back to the old IP 
address on Wednesday - I was on the phone with them on Thursday and it 
was corrected and pushed out to the root-level caches by Friday evening.  
However, some sites probably still had the fuct IP address in their cache 
for a few days, but by today it should be cleared up.  If you can't get 
through, use "taz.hyperreal.com" which will definitely work.

	Brian

Well, it might not help your pallor but I highly recommend a decongestant or
decongestant/anti-histamine the morning after.  It could just be me, but
having clear sinuses(NOT due to nose abuse by the way) can make you feel
worlds better and it just seems to help all around, not sure why.  My current
favorite is TavistD - works well, doesn't make you drowsy.  A natural version
would be echinacea - haven't tried yet.  Of course lots of orange juice or
the mega-every known herbal cure-fruit smoothie is good too.

Tam all day like me.

Well, there was enough people to fill the King St. dance floor but just 
barely.  The music had a few choice moments but was not as energetic as I 
had hoped with John Howard filling in for Garth.  It ended abruptly at 6 
a.m.  The highlight for me was that I tried out my new Moon Shoes, which 
are like trampolines you strap on your feet...  A cross between a 
moon bounce and platform shoes, a must for any raver with feet smaller 
than size 9...   They're fun and big attention getters, look for me 
towering over the crowd and bouncing around.

David

Wicked,

I showed up quite by accident.  Like the previous post said, kind of empty,
which
actually was a highlight given that I don't really enjoy wicked's because they
are
so crowded.  I loved the fact that everyone was friendly, lots of really nice
people
were there.  I love the smiles and hugs I got.  I really liked meeting Clinton
and
Joshua.   David your moon shoes were just the greatest.  In all it was an
unusual
way to spend Xmas Eve, and it will go down in my history books as very fun.

Ron.

Sorry... that was a message I posted on Monday, and I presume due to the

The Gardening Club is *NOT* happening tonight. It remains, as always, a

Space/Spundae et al on New Year's Eve--  Ambient/Dub/Jungle/anyhting goes 
with Synergy visuals and a jungle book environment.

Thanks to all who've been coming to support us...

Everyday is Christmas...
