Tim, Deaks and K-go practiced for almost twelve hours this week, they'll 
be spinning on six turntables and a sampler on Saturday for about 1.5-2 
hours from 11pm on.  
We are implementing plans to throw a free party if too many people show 
up at the indoor space so if you are coming and you get there to see a 
line outside stick with us you will have a party to go to (but bring your 
jacket! everyone)
If we ahve time we are going to build a dancefloor at the beach we are 
using :)
There is already a lot of firewood out at the beach to help keep us warm.
We also painted the floor of the theater we are using last night and it 
looks good.  
We hope to see you on New Year's Eve, but if you can't make it down I 
suggest you check out Begin Again!  that is our official alternative 
suggestion:)

Everyone please be safe and have a wonderful New Year's

From sfraves-owner  Fri Dec 30 10:44:10 1994

Received: from well.sf.ca.us (phred@well.sf.ca.us [198.93.4.10]) by nkosi.well.com (8.6.9/8.6.9) with ESMTP id CAA18531 for <sfraves@hyperreal.com>; Wed, 28 Dec 1994 02:35:08 -0800

Date: Wed, 28 Dec 1994 02:32:35 -0800
From: Fred Heutte <phred@well.sf.ca.us>
Message-Id: <199412281032.CAA14016@well.sf.ca.us>
To: sfraves@hyperreal.com
Subject: Great Tracks from 1994 (long)
Sender: owner-sfraves@hyperreal.com
Precedence: bulk

 
Best-of-the-year lists are traditional at this time of year.  I'm never
sure exactly what their value is, but it's fun and perhaps useful to take
a look back.
 
Even though I consider 1994 to be a year lacking in the classics that were
so prevalent in 1993 (the tracks that were overplayed at the time but still
sound good, ranging from "Show Me Love" by Robin S to "Acperience" by
Hardfloor to Orbital's "brown album," for example), I think this was a year
of significant deepening and development in all genres of house/trance/techno/
rave music -- what I've been calling "future dance music" for some time.
 
What was basically a truly underground music production and distribution
system has rapidly gone commercial (although hardly big potatoes in the
overall scheme of the music industry), as seen by increasing -- and sometimes
stiflingly so -- production and packaging values.  1994 was, among other
things, the year the dreaded 12-remix triple pack began appearing frequently
in record bins, reflecting trends that by the end of the year have many
people reconsidering the whole notion of remixing.  Remixes aren't going to
go away, but perhaps there will be more attention to quality and individual-
ity, and much less of the paint-by-numbers approach that has reduced the
overall quality of remixes by "name" producers while perhaps improving sales
for the short run.
 
I'm a very selective buyer (about 1.5% of what I hear, typically), and still
acquired about 150 titles with 1994 copyrights or probable release dates.
My tastes ran strongly toward the UK this year, though the West Coast and
Detroit are getting my attention a lot now too.  This time, it's all vinyl
but I just got a Denon 2000F so no doubt CD issues will be a high priority
in 1995.
 
Three full-length albums deserve separate mention: Dajae's "Higher Power"
(including "You Got Me Up" and many others with the amazing Cajmere on the
mixing desk), Orbital's "Snivilization" which keeps improving on every
listen, and for hands-down album of the year, "The African Dream," every track
a classic and I just wish the remainder from the CD were also on the vinyl.
The one and only time I'd argue for a triple-pack release!
 
Of course it's hard to be fair in a "picks" list, and obviously quite a lot
of great music is not included here.  But for a few laughs at least, here's
my Preferred Dozen, another Choice Dozen, and quite a few Mentionables . . .
 
 
Phred's Preferred Dozen: 1994
-----------------------------
Airfix - Stick To It (Eat Vinyl, Bob!)
  Tribal house with a pure hook.  The flip of the EP, "I Found You," is
  also excellent.  Eat vinyl, and love it!
 
Boiling Point - I Am (Nice'n'Ripe)
  Uplifting, no-nonsense vocal of the year.  The New Jersey mixes exceed
  the London ones here.  Like Obsessive, Nice'n'Ripe is an under-rated
  label which recently put out an excellent compilation.
 
Cygnus Loop - Nyhabingi (Snoek)
  House music for the future.  An airy, diffuse breakbeat suddenly crumbles
  down into a cosmic, light-stepping romp.
 
Deep Freeze Productions - Feelin' Dub (Sure Shot)
  Is it deep house?  Progressive?  Who *cares* about labels!  Superb and
  off-kilter blend of beats and vocal loops on a wicked bassline.
 
Deep2 - Sphere II (Phoenix)
  LA musicians and producers are starting to put out *great* tracks, and this
  is one.  I prefer this live side over the studio one.  Deep but never
  suffocating.
 
51 Days - Tracktion (Touche)
  More sounds from the future of house.  A compelling and memorable track.
  Touche is definitely a label to watch.
 
Good Strawberries - Eyes on a Summer Day (M&G, Polygram)
  How to take a pop hit and *not* ruin it with a selfish remix.  The Gat
  Decor Mix 1 balances the lyricism of the original with their driving sound.
 
Needle Park - Crossfire (Wesayso)
  My perfect 5:30 am track: the Totally Wired mix.  Totally tripped out,
  totally driven, totally shake-ya-groove.
 
100th Monkey - Nyika Nyika (Boomtang)
  Unique cross of African vocals and floating house beats.  Makes Deep
  Forest sound like the sad pastiche it really was.  The "Boomtang boys"
  continue to put out consistently fine tracks (c.f. the "Rose Garden"
  remixes).  Toronto: the hidden gem of North American house.
 
Sensation - Beautiful Morning (550 Music, Sony/Epic)
  The perfect track to follow Crossfire.  Fluke has some kind of Key to
  the Groove; they prove it again on the Magimix here.
 
Underground Resistance with Yolanda - Living for the Night (UR)
  One of the gems from my Detroit visit.  Credits: Reynolds, Banks, Mills,
  what else is there to say?  I like the "Free Mix."  Great Detroit techno
  soul with a superb vocalist -- there's a lot of this coming out now.
 
Sven Vath - Monk Trance (Soil Samples, WEA)
  Quite different from the bald one's other output; this stands, er, heads
  above with responsible overdubs of chanting onto a rock-steady
  trance groove.
 
 
And Another Dozen . . .
-----------------------
Blunted Chimps - Love, Music, Sex (Shindig)
  A great EP, along with "Get It On" and "Don't Need It."  Smart UK house.
 
C&B Club - C&B Volume One EP (Platform 12)
  My vote for most balanced house EP of the year.  All four cuts, "Movin,"
  "Choc Rok," "Don't Ya?" and "Get the Rhythm" stand out.  Just reissued
  domestically with a couple of lesser tracks -- stick to the original.
 
Sharon Dee Clarke - Runaway Love (Rumour)
  Serious Rope follow-up to "Happiness" featuring my favorite house diva.
  How to turn a mediocre song into a great track with superb production
  and singing.
 
Graylock - Rising Horizon (Mental Radio)
  Tuneful techno, or transformed house.  Kinda hard to say which.  Sticks
  in the mind wonderfully, though.  Works well anywhere in the mid-130 bpms.
 
Kamasutra - Night Walk (Disco Magic, Touche)
  Originally on two Italian 10-inch disks, a huge hit on Touche with five
  superb remixes.  I like "Black Horses" best, with its Santana-ish *solo*
  (imagine that, a solo on a dance record!).  The "DJ's favorite" of fall 1994.
 
Angelique Kidjo - Agolo (Island)
  As commercial as a remix can be but well beyond.  Check the MK 10 Dub.
  Not everything Mark Kinchen does holds interest, but this does an excellent
  job of transforming Kidjo's superb original (she easily made my best-of for
  1994 in African music) without losing the essence.
 
The Question - Everybody (Black Sunshine)
  A pastiche of classic house sounds and the big deep beat and tongue
  firmly in cheek all the way.
 
Rebound - Rock the House (Manchester Underground)
  Everybody including me went for "Make It Funky," but I ended up liking this
  even more.
 
Subterfuge - Knowledge (Shifting Gear International)
  More soulful future house; hits the *spot*.
 
Vibe Academy - Jus' Love (Tumblin')
  Hard beats, divine vocals.  Kinda hard to beat that combo!
 
Vibe Tribe - Dance With Me (DJ International)
  Smart and varied remixes.  I only have the test pressing so I'll say,
  play the first track on each side.  Chicago meets New York with a twist.
 
Susumu Yokota - Hi (Space Teddy)
  Almost a toss-up with "San" a close second on this excellent EP.  Insightful
  and tuneful ambient techno.
 
 
Persistent Mention...
---------------------
Astral Matrix - High Tide (O.O.B.E.)  entire EP is excellent trance acid
BKS - I'm In Love With You (Radikal)  almost 17 amazing minutes on the flip
Boom Generation - Sweet Slam (Eat Vinyl, Bob!)  the next chapter!
Canyon - Tumbleweed Reprise (Bellboy)  triposonic
Clanger - Strata (Seismic)  more tranced-out ambientish technoey housey...
Deep Piece - Torwart (Limbo)  consistently good label, consistently good track
Delirium - Flowers Become Screens, Return to Babylon Mix (Nettwerk)  dubbbbbb!
Eastmen - U Dub (Tribal America)  you dig?
Fuzzy Logic - Lekker Vet (Whoop!)  or Lekker Vet/Fuzzy Logic?  anyway: yesss!!
In 2 Deep - Last Night (A DJ Saved My Life) (white label)  funky & driving
Killa Green Budds - Keep Slippin' (Strictly Rhythm)  1994, Third Floor stylee
The KK Kings - Disko Inv-Asian (Big Life)  bhangra house?! you bet!!
Lady B - Yes It Is (F)  it is not possible... to describe this...
New State Crew - Release Yourself (Bubblegum)  uplifting
Paradox - Funky Revolution (Strawberry)  people! power! yeow!
Peyote Dreams - State of Mind (Rhythm Design)  tribal tribal tribal
Roger S - Yes I Do (Freeze)  you better believe I do!
St Germain-en-Laye - Walk So Lonely (F)  *blues* house, unique and *good*
Shape Changer - Crystal Dreams Vol. I (Experimental)  excellent; great label
Sound Factory - Good Time (Logic)  as good as commercial house can be
Swag Bag - The Money EP (Higher State)  five innovative coins o' the realm
Technova - Tantrum (Sabres of Paradise)  my fave of the entire Sabres list
Todd Terry - Jumpin' (Freeze)  first two-thirds is hard house track of the year
3 Man Jury - Digital Autopsy (Kickin')  swirling acid
Triplepack - Join Hands (Urban Hero)  the We Are Family riff in a new galaxy
Trybet - Five Elements (Defective)  like Armani meets Atkins, maybe
Wintermute - Bushman (Skunk)  classic tribal excursion
 
 
A salute to you all for 1995, and remember . . .
 
  * * *  The sound is universal, but keep it underground and true.  * * *
 
 
"see you in the future"
 
phred
 
Portland, Oregon
28 December 1994

Hello everybody...well, it's now the day before New Year's Eve, which,
by the way, you may have noticed, happens to fall on the evening of the
(um, morning...) of a new moon.

In honor of this event, the New Moon crew are doing the ambient room at
Begin Again, which will probably be the "undergrounded-est" of all the
newyearseve events this year.  Which means, lots of groovy people, lots
of FRESH dj's...but no underground event would be complete without YOU,
the Sfravers who believe in the "do it yourself" ethic.  

If you want to help us "do it up right" in the ambient space (which looks
like it's going to be ENORMOUS) please email me or gregg (gregg@fly1.berkeley.
edu) or just give us a call (voicemail: 415-267-3076, notvoicemail: 510-
525-7780).  We want to try for that sucks-you-into-the-deepest-of-chills
effect achieved at the Albany New Moon not long ago.

open invitation:  bring something for the altar, food and water to share,
a pet! (jus' kiddin') and something soft to rest your tired body on when
you just cain't dance no more....  also, if you still have it, bring your
list of lastyears newyears resolutions!  (to be ritually burned)

an' i want to say to everybody out there who've brought their beautiful selves
to newmoon events in the past:  thankyou for making 1994 the happiest in my
entire life!


love and kisses,

ann
